The Yongding River Breach Has Not Been Blocked, and the North Canal Has Also Breached; All Rivers in the Suburbs of Tianjin Are Flooding; Authorities Urgently Order Personnel to Defend

(Tianjin) The North Canal breached at Beicang at 12:00 PM on the 28th, and the water overflowed, inundating twelve villages along the embankment. Chen Zhongyue, the Magistrate of Tianjin County, personally led a team of laborers and police to rush to block the breach at 2:00 PM in the afternoon. The Yongding River breach has not been blocked, and water is overflowing from Shuangkou Town. The roots of the levee on the south bank of the Sanjia Dian have been soaked. The Yongding River Bureau of the North China Water Conservancy Commission supervised workers to build a dam all day on the 29th. The north bank was not affected. The dredging work on the Hai River has not stopped. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The water level of the rivers in the suburbs of the city has risen. Li Yinqiu, the Deputy Director of the Public Works Bureau, and Chen Zhongyue, the Magistrate of Tianjin County, went to inspect the embankments of various rivers on the 28th and supervised the personnel to repair and block the damaged areas. The [Hai] River has risen sharply. There has been continuous rain in the upper reaches, and mountain torrents have erupted, causing the water level to rise sharply. All river ships have been suspended. (28th Special Dispatch)

Japan's Establishment of a Consulate in Chengdu Has Not Yet Been Proposed

Change in Date of Japanese Fleet Maneuvers in Fujian Waters

(Xiamen) The Japanese Combined Fleet's maneuvers in the Fujian waters were originally scheduled to arrive in Xiamen on August 1st and conduct attack and defense exercises near Xiamen. Tianjin Customs Tightens Crackdown, Smuggling by Ronin Gradually Decreases

(Tianjin) Smuggling outlets are nearing their end. Ronin have suffered heavy losses due to large quantities of goods stored in a certain concession in Tianjin. The Ronin have approached Tianjin Customs to pay two-fifths of the customs duties to obtain tax receipts and be allowed to transship the goods to the south. The Customs authorities have refused, citing that there is no such precedent. Tianjin Customs has been cracking down severely in recent days, and smuggling has gradually decreased. The verification and issuance of transshipment tax receipts at the station are busier. Due to smuggling, the tax revenue of the Tianjin and Qin Huangdao Customs in North China in the first half of the year was only over 12 million, more than 9 million less than the same period last year. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the 28th, a ronin, Li Wuxing, attempted to transport more than a thousand silver dollars in four packages and a handbag from Tianjin to the south. He was caught by customs officials at the main station, and the items were confiscated. The ronin was sent to the Japanese consulate. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) From the 27th to the 28th, 200 bags of sugar and over a hundred pieces of cloth were transported from Nandaisi and Changli to Tianjin in small shipments, destined for a certain concession. As the customs authorities still have no concrete measures for cracking down on smuggling at the station, they were allowed to be moved away. (28th Dispatch)

Tensions Between Britain and Japan over China Issue Intensify; Britain Opposes Japan's Expansion of Spheres of Influence in China; Japan Requests Start of Negotiations for Mutual Understanding

(Tokyo) Tensions between Britain and Japan have intensified recently due to the China issue. The Japanese government is extremely concerned about eliminating this animosity. Yesterday, the Japanese government received an important report from Yoshida Shigeru, the ambassador to Britain. It is reported that the report stated that the British government, on the one hand, is maintaining its vested interests in China with an unyielding attitude and intends to use its influence to bring eastern Hebei and Peiping under the legitimate jurisdiction of the central government. On the other hand, it opposes Japan's policy of expanding its spheres of influence in China and demands that Japan reconsider various specific issues in Manchuria and North China. After considering this report, the Japanese government believes that it is imperative to start negotiations with Britain on the China issue and trade issues in various British territories. Then, based on mutual political understanding, an agreement can be reached. It is also reported that the Japanese government intends to explain to the British government that: 1. Japan has no ambition to invade Chinese territory. 2. Japan naturally respects Britain's vested interests without any doubt. As for Japan's so-called special position as a force for stability in the Far East, it still requests the understanding of the British government. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Dispute Arises Among Japanese Businesses over the Sale of the Tianjin Huaxin Cotton Mill

(Tianjin) Funatsu Tatsuichiro, the executive director of the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China, arrived in Tianjin on the 28th to investigate the state of the cotton yarn industry in North China and to negotiate the purchase of the Huaxin Cotton Mill on behalf of the Toyo Cotton Spinning Company. The Huaxin Cotton Mills in Qingdao and Weihui have both placed advertisements in Tianjin stating that they are not related to the Tianjin Huaxin Cotton Mill and have no intention of selling shares. This proves that only the Tianjin mill is for sale. Both the Kanegafuchi Spinning Company and the Toyo Cotton Spinning Company have offered 1.2 million, leading to disputes. The matter has been submitted to the Japanese Consulate General for instructions. Some shareholders of the mill intend to carry out a buyout, but are hesitant due to various concerns. The Tianjin Qingfeng Wheat Flour Company, which is under the custody of a syndicate of creditors, is now being considered for purchase by the Manchurian Flour Milling Company, which has offered 240,000. British Interests in North China Are Significant; Embassy in Peiping Will Not Be Abandoned, but the Office in Nanjing Will Be Expanded; Senior Embassy Officials Will Reside There for Extended Periods Each Year

(London) During a meeting of the House of Commons today, Conservative Party member Lamb inquired of the government about the issue of moving the British Embassy in China to Nanjing. Foreign Secretary Eden provided a written response, stating: "In Nanjing, housing has already been secured that is sufficient for the ambassador and one secretary to reside in. The ambassador often spends extended periods of time in Nanjing each year. If the ambassador is not in China, the embassy counselor will be stationed in Nanjing as a substitute. However, I do not currently know when the embassy staff will be able to fully relocate to Nanjing, as this depends on the progress of the embassy's construction project. But as of now, a site has not yet been found. As it stands, Britain maintains significant interests in North China, and it is appropriate to maintain the embassy in Peiping and not abandon it." Japan's Relationship with Britain; Attempt to Start with Commercial Issues; And Seek to Adjust the Entire Relationship

Goods Sent by Mail Should First Obtain a Sales and Transportation License

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has received reports that unscrupulous merchants in various places are packaging imported goods that should be inspected as parcels and sending them by mail. If inspections are not carried out uniformly, postal transportation will become a hotbed for smuggling. In order to strictly prevent smuggling, in addition to already notifying the Ministry to instruct all post offices to require merchants shipping imported goods that are legally subject to inspection to present a sales and transportation license before allowing them to be shipped, the Ministry has also recently instructed all customs offices that if merchants ship imported goods that are subject to inspection by mail, they should be required to first submit evidence of tax payment to the customs and obtain a sales and transportation license before allowing them to be shipped; otherwise, they should be detained and confiscated. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

It is reported that the majority of the funds will be used to construct the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway, with the remainder being used to develop cotton weaving, sericulture, mining, and electrical power, among other projects. (28th Special Dispatch)

Many Bags of Private Sugar Seized in Xuzhou Port

(Xuzhou) The Customs Resident Inspection Office in Xuzhou has seized a large number of smuggled sugar in recent days. 166 bags from Fuki in Xuzhou Port and 50 bags from Tongdexiang in Peixian were all transported to the General Office in Nanjing for disposal on the 28th. Spot checks are also being carried out in sections at various small stations to crack down on small-scale smuggling and prevent the source of smuggling. (28th Special Dispatch)

The National Government issued an order on the 28th appointing Luo Shouyi as the Administrative Inspector of the First District of Hunan Province, Wei Daofeng as the Administrative Inspector of the Second District, Yu Fanchuan as the Administrative Inspector of the Third District of Hunan Province, and Zhang Qixiong as the Administrative Inspector of the Fourth District of Hunan Province.

This order also states that Liang Guanying, the Commander of the 32nd Division, will be appointed to another position and should be relieved of his current position.

Travelogue of Japan (IX)

— Our Correspondent Hu Zhongchi, Hu Yizang

(8) Osaka Castle

In the afternoon, I received a visit from Consul Ren at the hotel. He invited us to visit Osaka Castle.

Osaka Castle was built by Toyotomi Hideyoshi, an unparalleled national hero in Japanese history. He invaded Korea and defeated the Ming army. The ambition of the Japanese nation to expand to the continent may be said to have been inspired by his military achievements. Since 1585, when he conscripted tens of thousands of civilians to build this unprecedentedly strong stone castle, his prestige not only intimidated all the islanders, but even shocked the Chinese court at that time. The Shenzong Emperor of the Ming Dynasty, fearing that he would invade the border again, wanted to deal with him with a policy of appeasement. Therefore, he sent Zhengshi Yang Fangheng and Deputy Envoy Shen Weiyi to cross the sea to Japan. These two envoys presented a golden seal and delivered a letter of credence to Toyotomi Hideyoshi in Osaka Castle. The most important sentence in the letter of credence was: "Specially bestow upon you the title of King." Little did they know that Toyotomi Hideyoshi completely looked down on our great power. He was furious when he heard about the conferment and rebuked the Ming Dynasty emperor in front of the Chinese envoys. When the two envoys, Fang and Shen, returned in dismay, the Ming Dynasty emperor knew that he had lost face, but there was nothing he could do. This historical story is most boasted about by the Japanese, and it is specially emphasized in elementary school textbooks. However, from the perspective of us Chinese, isn't this the first chapter in the history of China's failed diplomacy with Japan?

In addition to such a historical significance, Osaka Castle also has a more important, geographical—and still can be said historical—significance. We must know that the Osaka of today, which is so prosperous, was originally a barren land in the 16th century. After Toyotomi Hideyoshi built this castle, Osaka laid the foundation for the city. Since then, this city has gradually developed and finally became the center of Japanese capitalism.

Today's Osaka is full of magnificent buildings that demonstrate the power of mechanical civilization, but the Osaka Castle, which was built entirely by human labor 350 years ago, cannot but make us marvel. This castle is entirely made of large stones. The several pieces embedded next to the city gate are particularly surprisingly large. At that time, we in the mechanical age really cannot understand how the people under Toyotomi Hideyoshi purely used physical strength to move so many heavy stones from the mountains from afar and pile them up so neatly and seamlessly.

(Note) There are four famous giant stones in Osaka Castle: (1) Tako Stone, 8 meters high and more than 11 meters wide, located on the east side of the inner city gate. (2) Furisode Stone, 4.5 meters high and more than 13 meters wide, located on the west side of the inner city gate. (3) Dragon Stone, located on the east side of the outer city gate. (4) Tiger Stone, located on the west side of the outer city gate. The Dragon and Tiger Stones are each 4.5 meters high and 6.5 meters wide.

Most of Osaka Castle, including the square outside the castle, has been designated as a park. Five years ago, the citizens of Osaka donated 1.5 million yen to establish this park as a memorial project for the enthronement of Emperor Showa. Therefore, not only are there pleasing green shade and lawns everywhere inside and outside the castle, but also a newly built Tenshukaku (castle tower) in the Momoyama style stands majestically inside the castle, adding more interest to the people who visit the castle.

This ancient castle, which is open to the public for sightseeing, has been the battlefield for several battles in history, but today it still seems to be a military location permeated with killing intent. As soon as we entered the castle, we saw two Western-style buildings on the left and right, with signs reading "Army Arsenal Branch Factory" and "Arsenal." Further in, we saw the headquarters of the Fourth Division. This tall, four-story, yellowish-brown Western-style building seemed to be looking down on the opposite, purely Japanese-style, noble Kishu Goten (Kishu residence). A Japanese-style garden is opened in front of the palace, with some rockeries and forest springs embellishing it. We walked straight along the garden path and up dozens of stone steps to reach the Tenshukaku.

The Tenshukaku is a majestic high-rise building with white walls, black tiles, and eaves of five stories and eight floors. A pair of fish-head-like ornaments, glittering with gold, are dazzling on the top of the building, called "Kin Shachi." It is said that this architectural style from hundreds of years ago was borrowed from a painting on an ancient screen depicting the battle of Osaka Castle. However, this is only the appearance. Once inside, one feels that it is a very strong modern building built entirely of steel and reinforced concrete. We bought tickets downstairs and went up by elevator. At the top floor, we leaned on the railing and looked out at the scenery on all sides for a while. Then we went down to visit the exhibits on each floor. These exhibits are all relics from Osaka's history, including clay figurines and ancient pottery from prehistoric times, various artifacts from the founding era, many portraits of local sages, various calligraphy and paintings by famous people of the past, and astronomical telescopes imported from the Netherlands in the early days. Many of Toyotomi Hideyoshi's relics are well preserved there. What attracted the most attention were his banner, ancient helmet, ancient sword, and his excellent calligraphy. These ancient objects from three or four hundred years ago should make the general visitors recall the achievements of the hero who conquered the continent. However, we did not have such memories. When we looked at the clothes, hats and cultural relics of the founding era, we only felt how great was the grace that Japan had received from Chinese culture.

Annual Meeting of the Sino-German Cultural Association

(Nanjing) The Sino-German Cultural Association held its first annual meeting at 3 pm on the 28th. More than 30 people including Jiang Fuchong and Teng Gu attended. Jiang Zixiao from the Central Government and Guo Youshou from the Ministry of Education attended as representatives. Zong Baihua chaired the meeting and delivered an opening speech. It was decided that Shang Chengzu would report on the association's affairs. The representatives of the Central Government's Ministry of Education then delivered speeches in succession, and then discussed the proposals, all of which were passed separately. Finally, Zhu Jiahao, Jiang Fuchong, Shang Chengzu and other 14 people were elected as directors, (Central News Agency telegram on the 28th)

Polish Minister Returns Home on Leave

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, the Polish Minister to China, Wei Dentao, has been granted leave. He left Shanghai on the evening of the 26th and notified our Ministry of Foreign Affairs. During his leave, the affairs of the embassy will be handled by the embassy counselor Guo Leixin. (Central News Agency telegram on the 28th)

Japanese Academic Delegation Arrives in Peiping

(Beiping) A group of thirty-seven members of the Japanese Academic Delegation to North China, led by Professor Hashimoto of Kyoto University, arrived in Peiping from Tianjin this morning. In the morning, they visited the garrison headquarters, the Japanese Embassy, the Peiping Municipal Government and other places. In the afternoon, they visited various scenic spots and historical sites. Qin Dechun hosted a banquet at the Municipal Government that evening. The delegation plans to stay in Peiping for five days and go to Tongxian, Gubeikou, Zhangjiakou and other places for investigation. They will leave Peiping for Jinan on August 1st. (Special telegram on the 28th)

British Foreign Secretary Announces the Abolition of the Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Agreement Italian Government Guarantees No Retaliation Five-Nation Conference Resolves the Overall Situation

(London) The House of Commons met this afternoon to examine the Foreign Office budget and discuss the government's foreign policy. The meeting place was full, and the galleries were also crowded. Foreign Secretary Eden rose to speak and announced that the mutual assistance arrangements established by the Mediterranean coastal countries in December last year had no reason to continue under the current situation, especially because of Italy's attitude. The Foreign Secretary began speaking at 4:05 pm and finished after one hour and twenty minutes. First, he briefly described the main international problems and expressed optimism about the current situation. He said that if the future five-nation conference were to be held, it would be very beneficial to the future of resolving European problems. He also said that the British government does not want to raise the issue of the transfer of League of Nations mandated territories for the time being, but is willing to study the issue of re-allocating raw materials. As for the problems in certain parts of Europe that Britain is more concerned about, it is indeed true, but it does not ignore the events that occur in other parts of Europe, because once war breaks out, it will inevitably involve the whole of Europe and cannot be limited by region. After Eden finished speaking, Sir Sinclair, the leader of the opposition Liberal Party, expressed satisfaction with what Eden said. Former Foreign Secretary Sir Chamberlain attacked German foreign policy, and finally Foreign Secretary Eden concluded the debate. The opposition Liberal Party proposed an amendment to reduce the external expenditure. The House rejected the amendment with 290 votes against 143 votes, and passed the original external bill with 313 votes against 138 votes. (Havas telegram on the 27th)

British King and Prime Minister Cancel Summer Vacation

(London) Since King Edward VIII canceled his plan to vacation in the French Riviera, British Prime Minister Baldwin also announced yesterday that he would abandon his plan to spend his holiday in Aix-les-Bains on Thursday and will remain in the country to work. The coincidence of the simultaneous changes of the British King and Prime Minister, coupled with the fact that British Foreign Secretary Eden solemnly stated in the House of Commons yesterday when debating the Foreign Office budget that the international situation is complicated, has caused much speculation in the Parliament about the current situation. It is generally believed here that Baldwin's change of plan is related to Eden's serious speech, especially his statement that he has not yet fully developed the government's preconceived notions is attracting more attention. It is also believed that no adventures will occur in any aspect in the next few months. Regarding the King's decision not to go to the Riviera, there is no official explanation. (Reuter telegram on the 28th)

(London) After the Parliament adjourns at the end of this week, it will reconvene on October 29th. At that time, an adjournment will be announced again. The next parliamentary session is scheduled to begin on November 3rd. During the parliamentary recess, all cabinet members will remain in England. Prime Minister Baldwin must convene a cabinet meeting in August to consider international issues. He has canceled his trip to Aix-les-Bains. After receiving the reply from the German and Italian governments accepting the invitation to participate in the Locarno Five-Power Conference, he must make careful preparations through diplomatic channels. Furthermore, when the League of Nations General Assembly meets in September, it will discuss the future of the League of Nations, which the government also attaches great importance to. (Reuter telegram on the 28th)

(London) When Foreign Secretary Eden delivered his foreign policy declaration in the House of Commons this afternoon, he announced the list of British delegates to the League of Nations General Assembly, which will be held in September this year: Lord Halifax, the Lord Privy Seal, Malcolm MacDonald, the Secretary of State for Dominion Affairs, and Eden, the Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs, as the principal delegates, and Morrison, a finance official, Shakespeare, a health official, Lord Cranborne, a foreign affairs official, and Malkin, a foreign affairs advisor, as assistant delegates. (Havas telegram on the 27th)

(Rome) After British Foreign Secretary Eden delivered a speech yesterday announcing the withdrawal of the Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Agreement, although official sources did not express any opinions, public opinion was quite approving. Political figures expect that Italy will soon agree to participate in the future five-nation conference. (Havas telegram on the 28th)

Britain Expands Army Secretary of War Announces Conscription Plan

(London) The War Department, in view of the shortage of regular army recruits, announced in the House of Commons today by Secretary of War Cooper that it plans to train new infantry units from the supplementary reserves, limited to 17,000 initially. These infantry soldiers will serve for six years in the infantry and may serve for another four years at will. Nationals between the ages of seventeen and twenty-five who are unmarried are eligible to be conscripted. All recruits will receive 26 weeks of training in the first year, and then 14 days of training each year. All clothing will be provided free of charge by the government. During the training period, they will be paid according to the official infantry pay scale, and will also receive an annual gratuity of six pounds. (Reuter telegram on the 28th)

British House of Commons Discusses Foreign Policy Foreign Office Budget Passed

(London) The House of Commons debated the Foreign Office budget yesterday. Foreign Secretary Eden explained the complexity of the international situation, saying that since Germany reoccupied the Rhineland, the British government has tried to start negotiations to stabilize the overall situation in Europe. With this spirit, the British government submitted a list of questions to the German government in March. These questions were neither harsh nor far-fetched, but expressed a sincere attempt to facilitate progress. If the British government had received a concrete reply earlier, it would have saved a lot of time. The Locarno three-nation conference held in London recently was also based on the same spirit. He dared to say that the results achieved at the London conference could show that the three countries had a completely constructive purpose. The reason for this result was largely due to the far-sighted political talent of the French and Belgian authorities and their generous cooperation. The communiqué issued at the end of the conference proved that we are now focusing on the future, not just on the past. The British government is willing to support the establishment of a new Locarno understanding to promote a general solution in Europe. France and Belgium share this feeling. He hopes that the letters to the German and Italian governments will receive a satisfactory reply. Before the five-nation conference is convened, a lot of preparatory work must be completed through diplomatic channels so that the conference can achieve beneficial results. Although there are still many obstacles to be removed, we have reached a point where there is a genuine spirit of cooperation among the countries concerned.

The Foreign Secretary then described the new Straits Convention established at the Montreal Conference, saying that the most important lesson of the conference was that revising treaties by negotiation and agreement in accordance with ordinary procedures and principles of international relations can establish a solution that is more favored by all parties concerned than unilaterally denying treaty obligations. The conference has indeed enabled the British government and the Turkish government to achieve a closer and more harmonious understanding. The Foreign Secretary then described the League of Nations reform, earnestly stating that the government's purpose is to expand and consolidate the foundation of international cooperation, but the detailed measures are still not convenient to be announced now, for fear of hindering the League of Nations conference to be held in September.

At this point, the issue of the transfer of mandated territories was raised, saying that this move involves the entrusted powers, and the British government has not yet consulted with other countries on this matter. However, from the British government's point of view, this issue will raise significant moral, political and legal difficulties, and a solution must be found. The Foreign Secretary concluded by saying that there are still many international problems that have not been resolved. The government hopes that no party will raise serious disputes among countries again. As for the issue of the average distribution of raw materials, if the League of Nations convenes a conference to discuss it, our government is willing to join the discussion. Eden then discussed the overall situation in Europe, saying, "It is true that our country has certain obligations to certain parts of Europe, but this does not mean that our country is indifferent to the events that occur in other parts of Europe and does not care at all. If a conflict occurs in Europe, can it limit the war to one corner without extending to the whole of Europe? Or is there another aspect of the problems we are encountering that must be mentioned, that is, none of the European countries are willing to fight for other countries today."

Eden finally mentioned the issue of armaments and criticized the attitude adopted by the opposition, saying, "The arms expansion plan that we have submitted to the House of Commons for approval will in fact not be used in any way that conflicts with the League of Nations Covenant and the Paris Pact, but only for the purpose of defending our country or assisting countries that have been invaded. From my observation, the time for arms limitation may come sooner than generally expected, because the economic burden of huge military spending on various countries is already unbearable and cannot be sustained for long."

Eden concluded by briefly elaborating on the major responsibilities of the world's democratic countries today. After he finished speaking, Sinclair, the leader of the opposition Liberal Party, took the floor and expressed satisfaction with what the Foreign Secretary said. Former Foreign Secretary Austin Chamberlain, a Conservative Party member, also rose to speak and strongly criticized German policy, saying, "Germany now intends to recover its pre-war colonies. It must be known that the German government, within its own country, still refuses to grant its own people civil rights, discriminating against and encountering them, even worse than slaves. If another nation is placed under the jurisdiction of this kind of government, I am unwilling to share the blame for the consequences. The policies pursued by Germany last year and its continued demands are all subject to criticism. Our country, under certain circumstances, may have to join the war. We may as well explain these circumstances, namely (1) the scope of our self-defense includes the defense of the entire British Empire, (2) the independence of the Netherlands and Belgium is closely related to the independence and security of France." Lloyd George, the former Prime Minister and leader of the Liberal Party, rose to defend Germany and criticized French policy, saying that France has greatly increased its armaments and built fortresses, which is why Germany has spared no effort to strengthen its military.

Finally, Eden rose to speak, bringing an end to today's debate, saying that the government has not prohibited the British port of Gibraltar from supplying oil to the Spanish fleet. When asked by a member of Parliament what attitude the government takes towards the amendment of the League of Nations Covenant, Eden replied, "We do not want to propose major reforms to the structure of the League of Nations. We are prepared to participate in anything that the member states of the League of Nations unanimously agree to adopt in accordance with the covenant signed by all countries." (Havas telegram on the 27th)

The Foreign Secretary described the unilateral declaration, expanding on the guarantees given to certain Mediterranean countries during the period of economic sanctions against Italy and the unstable period after the termination of sanctions, saying that he was pleased that there was now a special reason to declare that this unstable situation had come to an end. Around mid-month, the Italian government had spontaneously issued declarations to the governments of Yugoslavia, Greece, and Turkey, the contents of which were notified to the British government by the Italian Chargé d'affaires in Britain. This official document clearly stated that the Italian government had made extremely clear guarantees to the governments of these three countries, that the Italian government had never planned and is not currently planning to take any aggressive actions against the three countries to retaliate against their implementation of sanctions against Italy. The Italian representatives to these three countries also earnestly stated that the Italian government believes that the matter of sanctions has indeed completely ended and is convinced that all countries will enter a new era of mutual cooperation in the future, so he himself is very happy to acknowledge and announce that the British government believes that there is no need to continue the unilateral guarantees.

The Foreign Secretary expressed satisfaction with the new progress made in the British-Egyptian negotiations. He then briefly described the overall situation in Spain, saying that the country is still in fierce fighting after a sudden large-scale civil strife. How the future will be is unpredictable. The Foreign Secretary then elaborated on the plan to protect British nationals in dangerous areas of the country, saying that he had telegraphed the Spanish Foreign Minister and the Spanish government had replied accepting the plan, which he was comforted by.

Referring to the problem of Danzig, the Foreign Secretary highly praised Lester, the High Commissioner of the League of Nations stationed in the city. He then turned his words and stated the colonial problem, saying, "What is related to this problem is not only Britain, but also all other countries that have mandated territories entrusted by the League of Nations are also involved. As far as our government is concerned, the transfer of mandated territories will definitely raise serious difficulties in morality, politics and law, and the government has tried its best to find a solution, but it has not succeeded so far, which I can honestly say. There is more than one international problem that has yet to be resolved today. Fortunately, in recent days, these problems have been more hopeful of being resolved. At this time, if there is any problem that is enough to cause a serious international dispute, I hope that no party will raise it. As for the issue of equal distribution of raw materials, if the League of Nations convenes a conference to discuss it, our government is willing to join the discussion." Eden then discussed the overall situation in Europe, saying, "It is true that our country has certain obligations to certain parts of Europe, but this does not mean that our country is indifferent to the events that occur in other parts of Europe and does not care at all. If a conflict occurs in Europe, can it limit the war to one corner without extending to the whole of Europe? Or is there another aspect of the problems we are encountering that must be mentioned, that is, none of the European countries are willing to fight for other countries today."

Eden finally mentioned the issue of armaments and criticized the attitude adopted by the opposition, saying, "The arms expansion plan that we have submitted to the House of Commons for approval will in fact not be used in any way that conflicts with the League of Nations Covenant and the Paris Pact, but only for the purpose of defending our country or assisting countries that have been invaded. From my observation, the time for arms limitation may come sooner than generally expected, because the economic burden of huge military spending on various countries is already unbearable and cannot be sustained for long."

Eden concluded by briefly elaborating on the major responsibilities of the world's democratic countries today. After he finished speaking, Sinclair, the leader of the opposition Liberal Party, took the floor and expressed satisfaction with what the Foreign Secretary said. Former Foreign Secretary Austin Chamberlain, a Conservative Party member, also rose to speak and strongly criticized German policy, saying, "Germany now intends to recover its pre-war colonies. It must be known that the German government, within its own country, still refuses to grant its own people civil rights, discriminating against and encountering them, even worse than slaves. If another nation is placed under the jurisdiction of this kind of government, I am unwilling to share the blame for the consequences. The policies pursued by Germany last year and its continued demands are all subject to criticism. Our country, under certain circumstances, may have to join the war. We may as well explain these circumstances, namely (1) the scope of our self-defense includes the defense of the entire British Empire, (2) the independence of the Netherlands and Belgium is closely related to the independence and security of France." Lloyd George, the former Prime Minister and leader of the Liberal Party, rose to defend Germany and criticized French policy, saying that France has greatly increased its armaments and built fortresses, which is why Germany has spared no effort to strengthen its military.

Finally, Eden rose to speak, bringing an end to today's debate, saying that the government has not prohibited the British port of Gibraltar from supplying oil to the Spanish fleet. When asked by a member of Parliament what attitude the government takes towards the amendment of the League of Nations Covenant, Eden replied, "We do not want to propose major reforms to the structure of the League of Nations. We are prepared to participate in anything that the member states of the League of Nations unanimously agree to adopt in accordance with the covenant signed by all countries." (Havas telegram on the 27th)

Moroccan Rebel Army Crosses the Sea Again: Major Battle in Southern Spain, Government Forces Suffer Defeat, Situation Perilous, Nationals and Foreigners in the Capital Prepare to Evacuate

Gibraltar: Moroccan rebel forces, advancing on Malaga in mainland Spain, defeated government troops this morning in the area of San Roque, killing 300 government soldiers. Many were wounded. Government troops retreated into the mountains at the time, but returned in the afternoon to counterattack, spraying the rebel army with machine guns. Fierce hand-to-hand combat ensued, with no clear victor by nightfall. The British destroyer HMS Basilisk arrived here yesterday. The ship was fired upon while rescuing 28 British and 12 other foreign nationals in Almería. Afterwards, government officers boarded the ship to apologize. Refugees all described the situation in Almería as appalling, with murder and arson rampant. A report from the Moroccan rebel side stated that officers and soldiers aboard the government warship Jaime I had requested to surrender to the rebels after being shelled by them the day before, seeking food, but their request was rejected by rebel leader General Franco. (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Gibraltar: It has been learned here that government forces have retreated to Malaga today, but the rebel advance in the south is not consolidated. (28th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Madrid: The government claims its forces have been victorious at Segovia and Toledo, 40 miles from the capital. However, fighting has broken out at Estepona, 25 miles north of Gibraltar, as well as near San Sebastián and Irún. The government forces' victory in the Segovia highlands will surely contain the rebel threat to Madrid. Government forces anticipate a major rebel offensive against San Sebastián. The battle for Estepona between government and rebel forces has been particularly fierce. Government forces set fire to pine forests in the area to impede the rebel advance. The rebels suffered 200 casualties but ultimately drove back the government troops. Fighting is still ongoing and appears likely to continue for some time. Whoever has stronger reserves will likely prevail. Observers who flew over both front lines claim rebel reinforcements are continuously arriving, while the government forces appear to be receiving less support. (28th, Reuters)

(London) The fighting in Spain is currently taking place near Utiel, a key point on the main road to the northern Spanish resort of San Sebastián. The rebels aim to retake the area. Government forces have dug trenches in Utiel to resist the rebel advance. San Sebastián is also riddled with trenches and obstacles. Many women are joining their male family members on the front lines. According to official reports received in London, the situation in Barcelona has improved, but if rebel forces occupy Zaragoza, Barcelona may revert to a serious state. (28th, Reuters)

San Sebastián: Government forces attacked rebel barracks in Loyola today, capturing 400 soldiers, and then advanced on Navarre. (28th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Madrid: The diplomatic corps here, concerned about the precarious situation of their nationals due to the unrest in Spain, held a meeting at the Chilean Embassy. They resolved to establish a standing committee to assess the situation of foreign nationals and determine appropriate responses. The Spanish government has arranged a special "International Train" scheduled to depart from here on the 30th of this month, dedicated to transporting foreign nationals, especially British and American citizens, out of the country, and guarantees the safety of the train en route. However, three American citizens disregarded the dangers yesterday and traveled to Alicante; the government cannot be held responsible if something should happen to them. (28th, Havas)

Madrid: Despite repeated government claims of military victories, the U.S. Embassy here today received instructions from Washington to evacuate the 160+ American citizens from Spain if suitable transportation is available. The U.S. government is not responsible for their safety. Simultaneously, the Spanish government announced the recapture of Toledo and the Alcázar. The estimated number of casualties nationwide in this rebellion has now exceeded 19,000, with 3,000 deaths in Barcelona alone and 1,000 in the capital. The government has also issued an order declaring the warship Sevilla a pirate vessel, prohibiting it from flying the national flag and authorizing its seizure anywhere. The diplomatic corps met today and appointed a seven-member committee to arrange the departure of foreign nationals. The committee is chaired by the Chilean Ambassador, with two representatives from European, South American, and Far Eastern missions. The committee has requested the Spanish government to provide a special train and necessary protection measures. (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Spanish Government Hastily Deploys Warships to Intercept, Government Forces Burn Pine Forests to Impede Rebel Advance

Madrid: The Spanish government is currently preparing a major offensive against the main force of a rebel column entrenched in the highlands near Segovia, 40 miles from Madrid. Simultaneously, the Spanish fleet is steaming at full speed from Tangier to Estepona, 30 miles north of Gibraltar, to prevent another rebel column led by General Franco from advancing. General Franco is currently leading a large number of seaplanes and troops from Ceuta to Algeciras, attempting to dislodge government forces from Malaga. Each plane can carry 10-20 people. Pro-government forces in the Estepona area set fire to forests to prevent the Moroccan rebel army from advancing. Although rebels have been pushed back by government forces from Madrid, they have won minor victories in many cities. Hundreds of pro-government riflemen and armed workers were annihilated this afternoon by elite rebel forces at La Línea, just a few miles from Gibraltar. The rebels also suffered 60 deaths. This group had recently surrendered to the rebels but suddenly set out from Tarifa towards La Línea today, apparently aiming to attack the Moroccan troops there. The rebels hastily sent reinforcements from Algeciras by plane, and engaged the group in battle just a few miles from La Línea. After a long and bitter fight, the riflemen were completely wiped out. Heavy fighting broke out in Estepona early this morning, with reports of 600 soldiers killed and 1,200 wounded. Furthermore, an advance guard of 800 rebel soldiers encountered a militia and 100 armed workers at Guadacorte, killing most of them. In the battle of Estepona, an estimated 400 government soldiers were killed. Twenty communists imprisoned in the La Línea barracks were killed last night, and another twenty this morning. The British government and its embassy have been advised by the Spanish government to relocate from San Sebastián. British embassy officials have moved to the small town of Zarauz near San Sebastián. The U.S., Italian, Argentinian embassies, and Norwegian and Czechoslovakian legations have moved to Irún, while the French embassy has moved to Fuenterrabía. (27th, Reuters)

Northern Rebel Army Fails to Attack the Capital, Due to Inadequate Reinforcements, Retreat Appears Possible

Rebel Headquarters near Segovia: According to the Associated Press correspondent embedded with the army, if reinforcements do not arrive quickly, the Northern Rebel Army Commander General Mola's repeated plans to attack Madrid may completely fail. The siege of the capital has been lifted. A general retreat appears necessary to consolidate rebel positions. Moreover, since Sunday's shelling, the majority of rebel forces in many areas have collapsed. It is also reported that the government has consolidated its positions in the Guadarrama Mountains and secured new positions south of Madrid. Food supplies have also been secured, and there is no longer a fear of starvation in the capital. However, despite the setbacks, the rebel army still believes it can capture the capital within a week. (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Southern Rebel Army Headquarters near Burgos: According to a special dispatch from an Associated Press correspondent, 100,000 rebel soldiers have arrived south of Burgos. After being inspected by rebel General Cabanellas, they immediately boarded vehicles to attack the Guadarrama mountain passes. This army is fully equipped and largely composed of residents from Navarre. Cabanellas declared that "Our army now holds the advantage. Aside from artillery, the Madrid garrison has no regular troops to support the militia. However, the artillery and ammunition are limited. Once General Franco's Moroccan forces arrive, the northern and southern armies will launch a simultaneous general assault on Madrid, at which time the outcome can be determined." (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Airplanes Carrying Gold Bars to Purchase Arms

(Paris) A Spanish three-engine airplane, piloted by Guatelli, landed at Le Bourget Airport outside Paris at 11:00 AM today. The plane was carrying 1,260 kilograms of gold bars, equivalent to slightly less than 45,000 ounces. It is reported that a Spanish airplane carrying £140,000 worth of gold arrived in France the day before, supposedly used by the Spanish government to purchase arms. (28th, Havas)

Officials Resign from Foreign Posts

(London) Counsellor Conte of the Spanish Embassy in the United Kingdom has resigned and is scheduled to travel to Brussels this afternoon. He told reporters, "Due to the unfortunate civil strife in my country, I cannot, in good conscience, continue to serve in the diplomatic corps." (28th, Havas)

(Rome) The naval and military attaché of the Spanish Embassy in Italy announced today his support for the revolutionary army and recognition of the provisional government established by General Mola in Burgos. (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

Security Restored in Barcelona

Madrid: After days of fighting, Barcelona has begun to return to stability. A total of 370 people have died violently in the unrest, including many priests and nuns. 270 of them died on Sunday of last week, 19 on Monday, and 81 in the following days. Around 1,000 people were injured. Instances of looting were relatively rare, and no banks were threatened. The city's political power and transportation are currently controlled by various labor unions, primarily the anarcho-syndicalist CNT (National Confederation of Labour). While the Catalan Autonomous Government can still direct the CNT, the question of how the two can cooperate remains. The CNT currently possesses a large number of arms. The Autonomous Government of Catalonia is backed by the Catalan Autonomist masses. It is generally believed that an agreement will be reached between the two sides to unite and cooperate. (28th, Havas)

Barcelona: It was learned today that three columns of government troops dispatched by the Catalan Autonomous Government have reached the vicinity of Cervera and occupied the cities of Cabestany and Bellpuig, routing four rebel columns along the way and inflicting heavy damage. Simultaneously, the fourth column of government troops flanked Cervera from Aragon and occupied the city of Salinella. Government forces now control two railway lines, greatly facilitating transportation. Barcelona is currently very quiet and has almost returned to normal. Militia Commander General Cabanellas has warned his troops not to seek revenge or engage in other transgressions. (27th, Kuo Min News Agency)

(Paris) International observers are still hesitant to draw definitive conclusions about the outcome of the Spanish unrest. Currently, both government and rebel forces are establishing positions and engaging in minor skirmishes as a prelude to a final showdown. Our correspondent in Lisbon reports that conditions along the Spanish-Portuguese border have returned to normal, and trains are running as usual. A dispatch from Washington D.C. states that the U.S. Ambassador to Spain, Bowers, has arrived in Port-Vendres, France, after leaving Spain. He has telegraphed the State Department to say he will board the U.S. Coast Guard cutter Cayuga today and inspect the conditions of U.S. consulates along the northern coast of Spain as far as Vigo. A dispatch from London states that the National Executive Committee of the British Labour Party has issued a declaration stating that the Spanish working class is sacrificing their lives to defend democratic institutions, and the British labor movement should help them. In the name of the Labour Party National Congress, a donation of £1,000 has been made. A dispatch from Berlin states that the German Ambassador to Spain, Stohrer, has telegraphed the Berlin Foreign Office, stating that since Madrid is still peaceful, he has requested the Italian Consul General in Barcelona to protect all German nationals there until a German warship arrives. (28th, Havas)

Inventory of Cash Reserves in Beiping and Tianjin, Hebei-Chahar Political Council Sends Personnel for Inspection, Totaling Over 54.4 Million Yuan
