Fiscal Reorganization in Beiping, Increased Revenue from Various Taxes

Nanjing Correspondence: Since Mayor Ma took office, Beiping's finances have been carefully reorganized, and tax revenues have steadily improved. The details of the various reorganization efforts are described below:

Business Tax

Regarding the business tax, the Beiping Municipal Finance Bureau has established the following methods for improving collection: (1) Prevent tax evasion and underreporting of taxable amounts by dispatching personnel to conduct door-to-door surveys in various districts. Those who have not reported taxes are instructed to report them in accordance with regulations. The Bureau is assisted by the Bureau of Social Affairs, the Bureau of Public Works, and the Health Department. Whenever merchants apply to these agencies for business registration, the agencies notify the Bureau to send personnel to investigate. This has been quite effective, reducing the number of tax-evading merchants and increasing tax revenue. (2) Instruct all merchants to renew their licenses annually in accordance with regulations. Personnel are dispatched to inform merchants to renew their tax registrations on time in accordance with regulations. (3) Abolish the cooperative collection associations. Previously, the Beiping business tax was entrusted to the cooperative collection associations of various industries for collection and remittance. However, many of them failed to comply with regulations. To eliminate long-standing malpractices, a gradual abolition method is adopted. Of the more than 60 cooperative collection associations originally established, more than 30 have been abolished, leaving only about 20. The Bureau directly collects taxes from the abolished industries. After vigorous reorganization, tax revenues have improved. The abolition of the remaining cooperative collection associations is continuing in order to achieve uniformity. (4) Construction businesses are taxed on a short-term basis. All construction businesses that were originally taxed on a long-term basis are now taxed on a short-term basis. Taxes are levied at any time based on the construction cost of the projects contracted by the businesses, as notified by the Bureau of Public Works. This has proven to be quite effective.

Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax

Since the transfer of the tobacco and alcohol license tax to the Beiping Municipal Government in 1934, personnel were dispatched in the summer of 1935 to conduct a thorough investigation and make corrections in accordance with regulations. In the spring of this year, all tobacco and alcohol taxpayers were instructed to truthfully report their business conditions quarterly thereafter for verification purposes and to prevent opportunistic behavior. After this reorganization, there has been a decrease in those operating in violation of regulations, and tax revenue has shown an improvement.

Brokerage Tax

Currently, in the handling of the brokerage tax, in addition to strictly investigating the business conditions of various households and correcting them in accordance with regulations, and stipulating that newly applying brokerage firms must obtain a guarantee, existing brokerage firms must also provide a guarantee. Thereafter, the guarantee must be renewed once each year when renewing the license to ensure prudence. This has also been very effective. According to statistics, tax revenues in Beiping have increased as a result of the active reorganization. The total tax revenue for 1935 (July 1935 to June 1936) was 2,516,632.60 yuan, an increase of 308,628.56 yuan compared to the 2,208,004.11 yuan in 1934. In addition, the municipal property revenue for 1935 was 261,906.12 yuan, an increase of 36,446.44 yuan compared to the 225,459.68 yuan in 1934. The Beiping Municipal Finance Bureau is continuing the reorganization while implementing (1) strict assessment and collection, (2) efforts to cultivate the public's habit of paying taxes, and (3) the strict implementation of rewards for reporting hidden and evaded taxes, to ensure that all public funds come from the people and that the government's legal tax revenue increases daily. Regarding future plans, the Beiping Municipal Finance Bureau has roughly formulated the following:

1. Improve the method of collecting house tax. Regarding the house tax collection area in Beiping, in addition to the six tax collectors assigned to collect house tax in the Xiaguan and Pukou areas, the city is divided into 55 districts, each with one tax collector who directly collects taxes with official receipts. However, there are often tax-dodging households who use various excuses to delay payment, resulting in a large accumulation of arrears. In order to improve the method of collecting house tax, the Bureau plans to entrust banks with the collection of house tax in Beiping to cultivate the people's habit of paying taxes themselves. The method is to first select the bank with the most established branches, sign a contract with it, and specify the terms. The Bureau will directly notify each taxpayer of the amount of house tax due each period, limiting them to pay the amount in full to the nearest bank within a specified period. If payment is not made within the specified period, the Bureau will impose a late payment penalty separately to deter delays.

2. Re-investigate house tax. Since the house tax was re-investigated in 1934, two years have passed. During this period, due to the opening of roads, construction changes, and property rights transfers, although personnel have been dispatched to conduct detailed investigations from time to time, it is inevitable that there will be hidden situations due to the vast area. The Bureau is afraid that the house tax will be affected if the delay is prolonged, so it plans to select capable personnel to conduct a thorough investigation this year to eliminate concealment and increase tax revenue.

3. Improve the method of audit. The Beiping Municipal Finance Bureau's assessment of house tax is mostly based on the reports of the collection personnel. There is no way to assess whether there are any omissions or omissions. The Bureau plans to have the audit personnel compare the police household registration book with the changes in the Bureau's taxpayer households on a monthly basis. If there are any discrepancies, they will be thoroughly investigated to avoid delays and omissions.

4. Reorganize business tax. The Bureau has formulated the following reorganization plan: (1) Plan to send personnel to inspect the account books of various merchants at any time and affix a seal to prevent false accounts. The annual business tax payable by merchants in Beiping is based on the capital amount recorded in their account books or the amount of annual business income. However, cunning merchants often prefabricate false accounts in order to take advantage of the situation. To prevent this, the Bureau plans to send personnel to inspect the account books of various households at any time and affix a seal for identification and to prevent forgery. (2) Plan to implement investigation and registration of changes in merchants. There are many changes in the reorganization, addition, removal, closure, or new replacement of merchants. The Bureau, in view of the fact that without clear registration, audit will be impossible if the changes are prolonged, plans to make an investigation and registration form for distribution to investigators in various districts. Whenever there is a change, they will register and report it at any time for verification. (3) Plan to request the police department to notify the Bureau whenever a merchant closes down in order to recover the arrears. The Bureau believes that many merchants who close down do not report in accordance with regulations, and it is often impossible to recover their outstanding taxes. The Bureau plans to make a notification form and ask the police department to instruct the various bureaus to fill out the notification when merchants report their closure, so as to recover the arrears and avoid loss. (4) Hold brokerage firms responsible for reporting business tax. Currently, Beiping only collects business tax from merchants operating stores. Due to the difficulty of investigation, temporary business of merchants in the city and outside, such as grain, trees, chickens, ducks, and pigs, has not yet been taxed. The Bureau plans to order each brokerage firm to be responsible for reporting the seller's business tax in order to increase tax revenue. (5) Open the collection of business tax for various industries that should be subject to tax. The Bureau will plan to open the collection of business tax for the entertainment industry, real estate companies, and other industries that should be subject to business tax in Beiping in the future.

5. Investigate the tobacco and alcohol license tax. In order to thoroughly reorganize the tax revenue, the Bureau plans to implement a general investigation in the shortest possible time in order to be thorough and increase tax revenue.

6. Reorganize the brokerage tax. Regarding the brokerage tax reorganization plan, the Bureau plans to order the various brokerage firms to submit two photos of the firm owner when renewing the license in the shortest possible time and affix them to the brokerage firm and the guarantee separately in order to prevent the abuse of acting as a substitute.

Fujian Province Highway Main Lines Fully Completed and Open to Traffic —Totaling 2,226 Kilometers—

Fuzhou Correspondence: In recent years, Fujian Province has been vigorously constructing highways at an extremely rapid pace. The Fuzhou-Xinghua-Quanzhou, Zhangzhou-Tingzhou-Longyan, Yanping-Jianning-Shaowu, Shayong, and Hangfeng lines have long been successively completed and opened to traffic. According to statistics from the Highway General Engineering Office, the total length of main trunk lines in the province is 2,226 kilometers, with 942 kilometers having paved road sections, 718 kilometers having dirt road sections open to traffic, 133 kilometers under construction, 258 kilometers surveyed, and 75 kilometers not yet under construction. Branch lines total 4,078 kilometers, with 142 kilometers having paved road sections, 1,519 kilometers having dirt road sections open to traffic, 578 kilometers under construction, and 1,839 kilometers not yet under construction. In total, the trunk and branch lines combine for 6,304 kilometers, with 1,084 kilometers having paved road sections, 2,237 kilometers having dirt road sections open to traffic, 811 kilometers under construction, and 2,172 kilometers not yet under construction. It is estimated that the completed portion exceeds five-tenths or more. The mileage of the main highway lines in Fujian Province is listed below: (1) Zhejiang-Guangdong Trunk Line: Starting from Fengling (provincial border), passing through Pucheng, Yingtou, Jianyang, Jian'ou, Nanping, Shaxikou, Shaxian, Melie, Yong'an, Liancheng, Pengkou, Xinquan, Shanghang, and ending at Yanqian (provincial border), totaling 684 kilometers, with 322 kilometers of paved road and 362 kilometers of dirt road. (2) Beijing-Fujian Trunk Line: Starting from Fenshuiguan (provincial border), passing through Fuding, Ningde, Xiapu, Luoyuan, Xianglou, Lianjiang, Majiang, and ending at Fuzhou, totaling 351 kilometers, with 27 kilometers of paved road, 123 kilometers under construction, 126 kilometers surveyed, and 75 kilometers not yet under construction. (3) Fujian-Guangdong Trunk Line: Starting from Fuzhou, passing through Xianan, Honglu, Jiangkou, Putian, Fengting, Hui'an, Luoyang Bridge, Quanzhou, Tong'an, Jiaowei, Longxi (Zhangzhou), Changqiao, Zhangpu, Jiuzhen, Yunxiao, Meizhou, Sidu, Zhao'an, and ending at Fenshuiguan on the Fujian-Guangdong border, totaling 510 kilometers, with 322 kilometers of paved road and 188 kilometers of dirt road. (4) Fujian-Jiangxi Trunk Line: Starting from Fuzhou, passing through Baisha, Gutian, Yushan, Jian'ou, Fengle, Jianyang, Masha, Jieshou, Shaowu, Mokou, Heshun, and ending at the provincial border, totaling 356 kilometers, with 115 kilometers of paved road, 109 kilometers under construction, and 132 kilometers surveyed. (5) Fujian-Hunan Trunk Line: Starting from Siming (Xiamen), passing through Jiaowei, Longxi, Nanjing, Shuichao, Shizhong, Longyan, Xiaochi, Xinquan, Pengkou, Hetian, Changting, and ending at Gucheng (provincial border), totaling 325 kilometers, with 157 kilometers of paved road and 168 kilometers of dirt road. As for the Fujian-Guangdong branch highways, five routes have been designated: one from Wuping to Xinquan, one from Xisi to Jiaoling, one from Fengshi to Dabu, one from Pinghe to Raoping, and one from Zhao'an to Shantou. Except for the Wuping to Xinquan route, which has already been completed and opened to traffic, the other four routes are currently under accelerated construction and are expected to be fully completed and open to traffic by early August. (July 25th)

Taicang: Armed Fight Occurs in Pailou Market

Mu A-xiao and Zhu Jin-nu, boatmen of the third district, fifth township, third neighborhood of Pailou Market in the county, are half-brothers with the same mother. They are of poor character and have always been restless. Recently, while at home during the slack season, they stole a goose belonging to Qian Da-a-xiao from a neighboring village creek and cooked and ate it with their family. The Qian brothers are exceptionally fierce and did not dare to argue, becoming distant over time. Unexpectedly, the Lu brothers became enraged out of embarrassment and deliberately sought trouble. Suddenly, on the afternoon of the 26th, they gathered over seventy ruffians from Qianjing, Yiqiao, and other places and swarmed into Qian village, dragging Da-a-xiao out and brutally beating him. The villagers, feeling deeply indignant, started an armed fight. Many on both sides were injured. Qian Zhimmei and other residents of Qian village, fearing a major disaster, urgently telegraphed the responsible Fuqiao Township Public Security Bureau. Upon receiving the report, the bureau immediately dispatched Inspector Zhou to lead the entire squad of police to rush to the scene and suppress the situation. The main culprits, Lu A-xiao and Zhu Jin-nu, were captured on the spot. However, they were snatched away by the crowd during transportation. Qian Da-a-xiao was severely injured and on the verge of death. Villagers transported him into the city and sent him to Kunshan for medical treatment. The other injured individuals sought medical attention on their own. Fortunately, the Public Security Bureau maintained order effectively, preventing the conflict from spreading.

Jinshan: Yang to Hold Memorial Service

Yang Youjun, also known as Yang Zhong'an, the second son of Mr. Yang Daohong of Zhangyan, Jinshan, was a top student in the Accounting Department of the Shanghai Business College. He was proficient in English and Japanese, excelled in accounting, and was particularly skilled in music. Teachers and friends all highly regarded him. He wrote extensively, with his works appearing in newspapers and magazines. He had a published collection of children's letters, and two works, "China's Land Tax" and "Jiangsu and Zhejiang's Salt Tax," totaling hundreds of thousands of words, are indispensable reading for those studying the tax system. Unexpectedly, Yang Youjun suddenly contracted typhoid fever on June 8th and died in his Shanghai residence on July 2nd. Those who heard the news lamented his passing. The teachers and students of Shanghai Business College will soon hold a memorial service. A memorial service will also be held at the Yang residence in his hometown on August 5th.

Suzhou: Transfer of Prosecutors from the District Court

Zhang Minsheng, a prosecutor at the Wuxian District Court, has recently been ordered by the Ministry of Judicial Administration to transfer to Shanghai Special District Court as a judge. His vacancy will be filled by Zhou Zhenzhi. After receiving the order, Zhang has been handling the closing affairs and is scheduled to go to Shanghai to assume his new post at the end of this month.

Drilling Two Artesian Wells

Suzhou's water supply has yet to be effectively managed. The Construction Bureau is now planning to first drill two large artesian wells, one in the city center and one outside Changmen, each 300 feet deep, with a planned water outlet diameter of 10 inches. After the two wells are drilled, they can provide drinking water for 100,000 people daily.

Thugs Fight, Injuring Several

On the 27th and 28th, continuous gang fights occurred here, resulting in six knife injuries, two of whom are in critical condition. The cause of this matter was very minor. It started when Wang Ronglin and Yang Gensheng, lacquerers from Yinguo Lane, teased women in the park. Yang was arrested and sentenced to six days in jail by the court. Yang's friend, Li Pinren, who worked with Wang Wenfan, a lacquerer at the entrance of Shangshu Lane in Hulong Street, collected eight small silver coins from his companions and asked Wang to deliver them to Yang in jail for his use. However, Wang embezzled the money. On the afternoon of the 27th, Li and others confronted Wang at the Chunyuan Teahouse in Xuanmiao Temple and slapped him. That night, Wang gathered a group of people, each carrying knives, axes, and iron rulers, to Hulong Street to retaliate against Li. In the darkness, they slashed Li in the waist with an axe, creating a wound about six inches long, breaking two ribs and deeply penetrating the lung. Li fell to the ground injured, and the assailants fled. Wang was arrested by the police. The injured person was sent to Guangmin Hospital and is in critical condition. On the morning of the 28th at 11 a.m., a carter named Lü Jinbiao and others mediated between the two parties at a teahouse near the Dayang Bridge outside Xumen. Unexpectedly, a disagreement arose, and they drew daggers and fought again. The police arrived and arrested fourteen people, taking them to the Third Precinct. The injured included Lü Jinbiao (a carter residing behind the Sanshan Guild Hall outside Xumen) with knife wounds on his chest and back, Wang Jincheng (a carter residing outside Xumen) with a knife wound on his right hand, Li Guangshun (a tofu shop worker) with a knife wound on his head, and Fan Jinan (a mud plasterer residing at No. 5 Daxian Lane, Yangyu Lane, inside the city) with knife wounds on his head and face. Lü Jinbiao lost too much blood and was severely injured, and was sent to Guangmin Hospital for treatment. The remaining ten are being interrogated and dealt with at the Public Security Precinct.

Nanhui: General Overview of Road Administration and Vehicle Tax

The enthusiasm of local figures in this district for road construction can be said to be the best in Pudong and superior to other places. In recent years, the completed stone roads include Zhanghu Road (18 li long), Beilong Road (4 li long), Beiyu Road (6 li long), Zhangheng Road (15 li long), District Central Road (12 li long, road base completed), Weiyang Road (8 li long), Dehua Road (5 li long), Panliu Road (3 li long), and Panlü Road (3 li long), totaling over 70 li, with a total expenditure of over 40,000 yuan. Of this 40,000 yuan, aside from a loan of over 5,000 yuan and over 3,000 yuan from collected vehicle tax, all were donated by local figures. The government has never provided special funding. However, the constructed stone roads require covering with mud once a year, patching with stone chips every three years, and complete renovation every ten years. Temporary damage also needs to be repaired immediately, otherwise, they will become rugged and uneven, causing inconvenience to travelers. If they are not repaired for ten years, all the effort will be wasted. Therefore, vehicle tax is collected to fund the district's road maintenance expenses. At that time, carters in the Tangqiao area, misunderstanding the situation, even started a movement to refuse the tax. After repeated consultations with the car owners and carter representatives, especially regarding the demand for timely repairs to the stone roads, the situation was finally resolved after ten days. On July 3rd of this year, an order was received from the county government that the tax should be uniformly collected by the local donation collection office of the county, and personnel were sent to the district on the 8th to take over. However, the order did not mention how the road maintenance and this vehicle tax would be managed. After explaining the actual situation and the entire process of collecting the vehicle tax, a petition was submitted to the county government to forward it to the two departments of finance and construction of Jiangsu Province, requesting a clear order designating that the district's vehicle tax be used exclusively for road construction and maintenance in this district, and that the collected vehicle tax be kept in a special account, to be allocated based on actual road maintenance expenses. However, the county government and provincial departments have never approved this request. It is feared that the result of this petition will be another empty promise. Therefore, a general report on the road administration and vehicle tax situation in this district is presented, seeking fair public opinion to urge the government to realize the situation. If the provincial departments still refuse to approve it, then in the future, those enthusiastic about local public welfare will become apathetic, and the people's faith in the government may be lost from this point on. It is hoped that the government can consider the local situation and not ignore the people's earnest expectations, and not bear to see the stone roads of over 70 li deteriorate and collapse due to lack of maintenance.

Wuxi: Six Notorious Robbers Arrested

Zhang Rongxing, the leader of the Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, received a confidential report the other day stating that Chen Yong'an, a notorious robber with a history of crimes, was hiding on a net boat in the Yangchang River near Outang Bridge. He requested that a team be dispatched to arrest him immediately. After receiving the report, Team Leader Zhang immediately led the police to the countryside to arrest him and successfully apprehended Chen Yong'an. He also arrested Li Mingfu, Ding A-er, and Chen Chunhua, who were involved in receiving stolen goods, as well as boat mates Chen Zifang and Wu Dianchen, totaling five individuals. They were all brought to the bureau, where Clerk Zhang interrogated them strictly. Chen Yong'an and others confessed that in December of the 23rd year, they formed a group of four and robbed a night boat in Yangpo Weiyu. On December 5th of the 24th year, they robbed Jiang Wanfu's fishing boat. In the spring of this year, they committed four thefts. Clerk Zhang verified their confessions and ordered them to be detained to await transfer to the court for trial.

Six Killed in a Major Fire

Deng Zengquan, a resident of Deng Gengshang near Zha Jia Bridge in the seventh district of the county, was over fifty years old and made a living farming. His house, a three-bay structure, was in an isolated village. There were seven family members, both male and female, and they were fairly well-off. One night, the other day, around midnight, Deng's house unexpectedly caught fire, and a terrible disaster occurred. Before long, the flames burst through the roof, and the fire was so bright that it illuminated the sky and was impossible to approach. Upon seeing this, the nearby residents immediately rang gongs to alert others. The Zha Jia Bridge Fire Brigade rushed to the scene with water dragons to put out the fire. However, due to the intensity of the fire, their efforts were ineffective. It took two hours to extinguish the fire. All three rooms of the house were reduced to ashes. During the fire, six members of the Deng family were unable to escape and perished in the flames. Only his son, Yonggen, who was out watching a local opera performance, escaped the tragedy. The charred bodies have now been dug out from the rubble, and their bodies are dismembered, a truly tragic sight.

Changzhou: Implementation of Shop Tax Collection

The Wuyi County Government received an order to collect housing tax. After convening a meeting, it was decided to postpone the collection of residential housing tax. The Public Security Bureau was instructed to investigate and organize the shop tax. The Public Security Bureau then submitted the tax amount to the county for approval. After further review and confirmation, it was submitted to the province for approval and scheduled to be implemented at the end of this month. It is reported that after this reorganization, the actual monthly collection from the 78 townships in the county is 2,909 yuan and 6 jiao 9 fen. The Public Security Bureau has prepared a budget, deciding to use the increased 800 yuan per month to increase police salaries by 4,800 yuan, adding one yuan per month to each policeman's salary, purchasing firearms for 3,000 yuan, and distributing them to various branches to strengthen their forces. The remainder will be used for pilot police projects, and this has been submitted to the County Administration Council for decision and implementation.

Haimen: Public Official Imprisoned for Framing

Yan Xuecheng, a resident of Liu Zhou Township in the fourth district, and Wu Bao-xin, the owner of Hengsheng Tang Store in the county and city, were successively framed and extorted for 1,100 yuan by Dong Huibai, Long Baohua, and Cui Guanghua, inspectors from the Nantong District Tobacco Prohibition Supervisory Office, in collusion with Wang Jianliu, the director of the Haimen Liaison Office. The county government has investigated and apprehended Dong Huibai and Wang Jianliu the other day. The others are still at large. Yesterday (the 25th), County Magistrate Chen personally interrogated them. Dong and others confessed without denying it and were immediately put in shackles and imprisoned.

Haizhou: Township Head Gathers Crowd to Snatch Criminal

The Second District Office of this county recently received an order to conscript labor to dredge the Sijia Tang River. Since the start of construction, Chen Dun, Lan Ni Hong, and other townships have held biased views and refused to conscript labor, hindering the progress of the river project. The District Chief Li Shoutong petitioned the county government to dispatch Du Kuangbin, the Public Security Section Chief, to lead a security team to the construction site to supervise and urge completion by a deadline. Since Section Chief Du resided at the construction site, over 3,000 laborers from various townships have arrived and worked diligently. Recently, the projects allocated to Lianbei, Datong, Chen Dun, and Wenming townships seem likely to be completed as scheduled. However, the number of laborers from Lan Ni Hong Township is small, and the projects allocated to them have not yet reached five-tenths completion. The other day, the downstream section of the project allocated to the township was secretly dug open, causing river water to flood in and hindering the project. Section Chief Du and Zheng Huichang, the work office staff stationed at the site, ordered the laborers to quickly block the opening and pump out the water, and ordered Wu Bingyuan, the chief of Lan Ni Hong Township, to quickly double the number of laborers to arrive and complete the project as scheduled. However, Wu ignored the order. As the deadline approached, Section Chief Du, together with staff member Zheng and a squad of soldiers, went to Lan Ni Hong Street yesterday to arrest Township Chief Wu Bingyuan and escort him to the construction site. After leaving the street for about half a mile, dozens of strong men suddenly appeared in the market, each holding firearms, and chased after them, firing shots like rain. Du and others fled to Dazui Gang to hide. Unexpectedly, Qi Fengxiang and other village heads gathered 60 to 70 strong men, firing guns to intercept them and forcibly snatched Township Chief Wu Bingyuan away. Over ninety bullets for the保安隊 soldiers' Browning pistol were also seized. Du immediately reported the situation to the county government. Upon receiving the report, County Magistrate He dispatched First District Chief He to proceed to handle the matter overnight.

Nantong: Handling Land Registration

The declaration of urban land prices in Tongyi County has been completed, and the Land Administration Bureau is continuing to handle land registration, establishing registration offices in various districts. The process is progressing smoothly and is expected to be completed within the month. After this registration, the county will proceed to clean up field taxes to solve the county's financial problems.

Expansion of the District Court

The Nantong District Court has seen a sharp increase in civil and criminal cases. Presiding Judge Sheng Shizhen has added a third courtroom and has obtained approval from the Ministry of Judicial Administration to transfer Judge Jiang Liquan to Nantong to fill the vacant post. Prosecutor Liu Shiqing has been transferred to Shanghai, and Lu Qi has been transferred to replace him.

Gaoyou: Lake Bandits Search and Rob Grain Transport Boats

Gu Hengxing, Sha Zaichi, Han Otter Cat, and Gu Wancheng, four boatmen from Jianhe Tou in Xibeigang Township, northwest of the county, rely solely on transporting and selling grain for a living. On the 24th, after selling wheat in Youjiang, they were returning home and anchored their boats at the Hukou of Xiajia Bridge. Around 1:00 a.m., a bandit boat suddenly appeared, with thirteen or fourteen bandits who spoke with a northern accent. They boarded the four boats and thoroughly searched and robbed them. Fortunately, the money from the wheat sales had already been deposited at home. Only the clothes and small change in the boats, totaling over 100 yuan, were robbed.

Yangzhou: Teacher-Student Adultery and Abduction Case Sent to Shanghai

Wang Guisheng, a 27-year-old man from Pudong, Shanghai, was staying at the Dingtai Inn on Zuo Wei Street in Yangzhou, accompanied by a 14-year-old girl, Li Peilan. They ate and slept in the same room, appearing to be a couple. The next day, Li Jinbao from Shanghai came to Yangzhou, reported the two to the police, and took them to the Jiangdu District Court for questioning and detention. This morning (the 27th), Zhang Chunsen and Xu Tingju, bailiffs from the Shanghai Special District Court, came to Yangzhou to submit a document to the court and retrieve the prisoners. The court immediately opened a hearing and handed over Wang Guisheng and Li Peilan to the police for return to Shanghai to face charges. It is reported that Wang Guisheng and his father, Wang Xiji, were teaching in Pudong, Shanghai. Li Peilan was a student of Wang's and became romantically involved with him. Wang took over 30 yuan, and Peilan took over 40 yuan, and they eloped together, hiding in Fanshui. Because the money ran out, they sent a letter to the girl's aunt for help. The case was discovered the day before their arrest. It is said that after the elopement, the Wang and Li families had already filed lawsuits in Shanghai. After receiving the letter, her uncle, Li Jinbao, came to Yangzhou and reported the case to the police, who arrested them and detained them at the court, pending their return to Shanghai.

The River Embankment at Fogan Zhou is Critical

The river defense in Jiangdu County is the responsibility of technician Zhang Hanqing, under the instructions of the Construction Bureau. He has already prepared plans in sections, drawn up diagrams, and submitted them to the department. The river embankment in the areas of Gong Wuwei, Gong Liuwei, and Doutian Temple on Fogan Zhou is in a critical condition and in imminent danger. Yesterday (the 25th), the county specially instructed the responsible personnel to supervise the various village heads and community leaders in the area to strengthen the defense and report at any time to emphasize the importance of the river defense.

Jiaxing: Rice Crops Infested with Rice Borers

The rice crops in the four townships of Jiaxing are currently infested with rice borers due to excessive heat, causing the rice leaves to wither and die. The earliest rice has already reached the harvest stage, and the mid-season rice is in the ear-forming stage. The insect infestation has caused the leaves to yellow and wither. The farmers have reported the disaster to the township offices and farmers' associations and requested relief. The county farmers' association has learned of this and has sent letters to the various township farmers' associations, requesting a detailed investigation and report on the disaster situation of the rice crops to be submitted to the county government for dispatching personnel to assess the disaster and reduce the land tax. The county government has also drafted methods for eliminating the rice borers, ordering the various townships to implement them earnestly to eliminate the rice borer infestation.

Hangzhou: Aftermath of the Dinghai Fishermen and Salt Workers Riot

Over twenty suspects have been arrested in the Dinghai fishermen and salt workers riot and sent to the Hangzhou District Court for trial. It is now reported that Zhang Zhongli, the director of the Salt Transport Administration's Tax Police Bureau, has been dispatched to Dai Mountain to meet with County Magistrate Shen Pu and local leaders to discuss a plan for the aftermath. A propaganda team has been formed to go to the countryside to spread the word that the salt workers must provide guarantees within one week to abide by the laws and regulations and not violate them again. The salt industry credit cooperative has been canceled. The government's losses will be compensated by the fishermen and salt workers raising funds. A reward has been offered for the arrest of the instigators of the riot for strict punishment. At the same time, the Suinan and Jian'an patrol ships have been dispatched to patrol the waters of Dai Mountain to maintain order.

Local News

Interview with Wu Wentian, Section Chief of the Ministry of Industry: Continued Negotiations on Factory Inspection in the Concessions; Difficulties in Implementing the Municipal Council's Licensing System; The Principles of Politics and Diplomacy Should Consider Humanity; Hoping the Diplomatic Corps Will Reconsider and Not Persist in Their Preconceptions

Central News Agency: The factory inspection issue in this city has been negotiated repeatedly by the municipal government and the authorities of the Public Concession, and a draft agreement is about to be resolved. Unexpectedly, the Diplomatic Corps suddenly raised objections, and the issue has stalled again. Wu Wentian, Section Chief of the Labor Department of the Ministry of Industry, came to Shanghai on business and exchanged views with various parties. A reporter paid a special visit to him to inquire about everything, and he gave the following statement:

Draft Agreement Opposed by the Diplomatic Corps

The problem of factory inspection in the Shanghai Public Concession, after five years of negotiations, began in June of this year. The Municipal Council and the Shanghai Municipal Government jointly drafted a draft agreement on factory inspection in the Public Concession. Examining its contents, it can be seen that the Chinese government has made many concessions and, for the sake of the happiness of the majority of workers, has not hesitated to compromise with the Municipal Council. The Municipal Council also deeply understands the Chinese government's painstaking efforts and shows understanding. Therefore, the conclusion of this agreement is not easy. We were about to wait and see the implementation of factory inspection in the Concession, so that the lives of tens of millions of workers could be improved. Unexpectedly, according to reports, just as the agreement was passed by the Municipal Council's board of directors, the Diplomatic Corps considered that the agreement could lead to the abolition of some of the treaty privileges of countries with extraterritorial jurisdiction and demanded modifications. According to the Diplomatic Corps' opinion, the measures in the agreement could only be implemented in Chinese factories within the Concession and in factories of countries without extraterritorial jurisdiction. As for factories of countries with extraterritorial jurisdiction, they have the rights granted by the Yangjingbang Regulations, and the Municipal Council should handle inspection matters for these factories by issuing licenses, with provisions on the licenses to protect workers and inspect various matters within the factories.

The Diplomatic Corps' Opinion is Truly Unacceptable

Therefore, if the Diplomatic Corps' opinion is put into practice, it would mean that under one factory inspection agency, for the same country's workers in the same area, two different laws would be enforced simultaneously: (1) the Chinese Factory Law (applicable to Chinese factories and factories of countries without extraterritorial jurisdiction) and (2) the Municipal Council's License (applicable to factories of countries with extraterritorial jurisdiction). Whether this approach is fair is beyond debate. After all, the provisions of the license can never include all the contents of the Chinese Factory Law. At the same time, the abuses of the licensing system are well known. I recall that in 1932, the Municipal Council took advantage of the annual meeting of taxpayers to convene a special meeting to amend Article 34 of the appendix to the Yangjingbang Regulations, using the licensing method to obtain factory inspection rights. At that time, the Chinese people opposed it, and the Chinese government also expressed its non-recognition. Even the Municipal Council itself knew that there were various difficulties in issuing licenses and was unable to implement it. The past is not far away, how can we forget it? Now the Diplomatic Corps is bringing up the old matter again, using methods that could not be implemented in the past to implement them today. Who dares to guarantee that it will be effective?

Factory Inspection Seeks Workers' Welfare

From the political and diplomatic standpoint of the Diplomatic Corps' opinion, we are not in a position to comment. However, factory inspection is for the welfare of workers and is a social, economic, and humanitarian event that cannot be concealed by politics and diplomacy. The realization of that opinion would greatly hinder factory inspection in the Shanghai Concession, and the lives of hundreds of thousands of workers in the Concession would still have no possibility of thorough improvement. From a socio-economic point of view and a humanitarian standpoint, this cannot but be considered a great regret. If the consuls of various countries could personally visit the poorly equipped foreign factories in the Concession and see the suffering of the workers, they might be moved and change their attitude of adhering to politics and diplomacy. Moreover, according to historical concepts, politics changes with the tide of social economy. Today, when modern civilization and the rule of law are widely advocated, how can we allow people to disregard humanity? Furthermore, these countries with extraterritorial jurisdiction have a long history of factory inspection in their own countries, and their protection of workers in their own countries can be said to be meticulous. Extending this consideration to others, they should provide assistance to China, which is newly establishing factory inspection, based on their good experience. How can they use political and diplomatic pretexts to obstruct it and still claim friendship and cooperation? Who can believe that?

Public Opinion Supports the Implementation of Factory Inspection

In recent days, Chinese and foreign newspapers have commented on the Diplomatic Corps' opinion to overturn the agreement, with varying opinions and viewpoints. However, they unanimously believe that the implementation of factory inspection in the factories of the Concession is an urgent matter, and they agree that extraterritoriality is only a technical issue and should not be overemphasized. These recognized and correct views are the consensus of Chinese and foreign public opinion. The members of the Diplomatic Corps should pay attention to it! In short, the solution to the factory inspection problem in the Concession must be based on the happiness of hundreds of thousands of workers. Our government will continue negotiations, and there is still room for remedy in preserving the technical aspects of extraterritoriality. Therefore, we hope that the countries of the Diplomatic Corps can reconsider and not persist in their preconceptions, so that factory inspection in the Concession can be realized as soon as possible.

Newly Arrived Giant Airplane for Eurasia Flies to Yunnan This Morning

The China Eastern Branch reports that Eurasia Aviation Corporation's newly leased JU52 three-engine Junkers giant airplane from Germany's Lufthansa has completed inspection. This time, it is carrying a large number of passengers and mail to various places.

Two Notices from the Jianghai Customs

The Jianghai Customs issued two notices, No. 1532 and No. 1513, regarding the continued exemption of dredging tax on tax-exempt export goods and re-export goods from Shanghai for another year, and the requirement for domestic goods similar to imported goods requiring sales permits to obtain domestic goods sales permits when transported to various parts of the country.

Notice 1: Regarding the exemption of dredging tax on tax-exempt export goods and re-export goods, this Customs issued Notice No. 1458 on July 31, 1935. Now, in compliance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, all dredging taxes on tax-exempt export goods and re-export goods from Shanghai will continue to be exempted for another year from August 1 of this year. All merchants are hereby notified. Tang Haian, Supervisor, Baron von Rahden, Customs Commissioner.

Notice 2: Imported goods requiring sales permits were listed in Notice No. 1521 issued by this Customs on June 23 of this year. Now, in compliance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, all genuine domestic goods transported to various parts of the country that are similar to the imported goods listed in the aforementioned table and easily confused should obtain domestic goods sales permits. All merchants are hereby notified. Tang Haian, Supervisor, Baron von Rahden, Customs Commissioner.

Mechanical Industry Association Petitions the Ministry of Finance to Abolish Exorbitant Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies in Guangdong Province

The Shanghai Mechanical National Goods Factories United Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Regarding the long-standing imposition of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies in Guangdong Province, we earnestly request that a clear order be issued to abolish them in order to revitalize industry. Upon investigation, national mechanical goods manufactured in Shanghai and transported to Guangdong Province are all subject to heavy taxes. For example, an electric fan worth 25 yuan is valued at 50 yuan, taxed at 10%, equivalent to 20%. Moreover, various pretexts are created to heavily tax all manufactured goods. This spring, a special tax bureau for imported agricultural products and miscellaneous items was established. Although the name of the bureau clearly includes the words 'imported,' goods transported from other provinces to Guangdong must be heavily taxed by this 'imported' tax bureau before being released. Taking national rubber-soled shoes as an example, a dozen pairs are taxed at 60 cents. The taxation of other national goods can be easily imagined. Levying taxes in the name of taxing imported goods while actually heavily taxing national goods and exploiting the people is beyond compare. Previously, this association repeatedly submitted petitions to your Ministry requesting exemption, but the heavy taxes in Guangdong remain the same. The pain of industry has long been recognized. Now that your Ministry has sent a special commissioner to Guangdong Province to reorganize the finances, all the exorbitant and miscellaneous levies that have caused deep harm over the years should be promptly abolished in order to revitalize industry like a sweet rain. Therefore, we specially submit this document and earnestly request your approval to issue a clear order to abolish them. We eagerly await your decision."

Xu Fu Allocates Funds to Maintain the Shanghai Reconstruction Public Bonds; the First Quarter Principal and Interest for This Year Have Been Paid Off

The municipal government previously issued reconstruction public bonds to rebuild the war zone, originally designating the revenue from the Jianghai Customs pier as collateral for the principal and interest of the bonds. However, due to the recent decline in pier business, the revenue from the pier has been affected, resulting in a shortfall of tens of thousands of yuan in the principal and interest due for the first quarter of this year. However, the municipal authorities have always attached great importance to the credit of public bonds. Since Xu Fu became the Director of Finance, he has strengthened the reorganization of the city's finances, further consolidating the city's financial foundation. The tens of thousands of yuan that were insufficient for the principal and interest due for the first quarter of these reconstruction public bonds have been approved by the municipal government to be allocated from other tax revenues in full to maintain the credit of the bonds. National Goods Transported to Various Places Must Apply to Customs for Sales Permits to Prevent Imported Goods from Impersonating Domestic Goods

The China Times News Agency reports that the Inspector General of the Jianghai Customs replied yesterday to a letter from the Shanghai National Goods Factories United Association, stating: "Regarding your association's letter No. 1255 dated July 18, 1936, which cited a letter from the Huatong Electric Appliance Machine Factory stating that the factory's products transported to various places via the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways must be inspected by the Inspection Office, delaying the date, and requesting a letter of certification stating that the factory's products are indeed domestic goods to allow them to be released, etc., approved. According to the Provisional Regulations for the Inspection and Sales of Imported Goods, goods to be inspected that are sold domestically must apply for sales permits to be transported. The Inspection Offices established by the Customs at various stations must also inspect the goods to be inspected, even if they are domestic goods manufactured domestically, to prevent imported goods from impersonating domestic goods and being smuggled. Now, the government has stipulated that domestic goods manufactured domestically that are to be inspected must be reported to the Customs for the issuance of domestic goods sales permits when transported through the Customs to facilitate inspection and transportation. The Huatong Electric Appliance Machine Factory's products transported to various places via the two railways should comply with the regulations and apply to the Customs for domestic goods sales permits to facilitate inspection and release. The aforementioned information is hereby replied to, and we hope you will inform the Huatong Electric Appliance Machine Factory accordingly."

Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Petitions for Amendment of Income Tax Regulations to Change the Tax Threshold to 50 Yuan

The Municipal Federation of Trade Unions submitted documents to the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Regarding the Shanghai Sixth District Public Bus Industry Trade Union's petition requesting that the government be asked to change the income tax threshold to 50 yuan to alleviate the suffering of the people, it is reported in the newspapers that the Legislative Yuan has passed the Income Tax Regulations, which will be implemented soon. Taxes are the source of national finances and the obligation of citizens. If they benefit the country and do not harm the people's livelihood, they are happy to pay them. However, Item 1 of Category 2 of the regulations states that for those with an average monthly income of 30 to 60 yuan, the tax is 5 cents for every 10 yuan, which has a great impact on the livelihood of lower-level employees. We respectfully offer the following suggestions: Considering the high cost of living today, employees with a monthly income of 30 to 40 yuan bear the heavy burden of supporting a family of several people. They cannot refuse to support their parents, and they cannot abandon their children's education. They are already struggling to make ends meet by tightening their belts, and the decline of all industries brings the fear of unemployment. How can they bear any unexpected burdens? The foundation of the nation is to nurture the people. Taxing the poor does not contribute much to the national finances, but it causes great suffering to the people. We feel uneasy and cannot remain silent. We respectfully request that your esteemed association forward this petition to the government, earnestly requesting that you consider the difficulties of the people and grant an amendment to change the tax threshold to 50 yuan. We are extremely anxious to hear your decision." According to this, the hardship of lower-level employees is undeniable today. The points raised by the association are all based on facts. In addition to submitting separate reports, we are specially submitting this document to your esteemed Yuan (Ministry) requesting that you approve a request to the Legislative Yuan to amend the income tax threshold to 50 yuan to alleviate the difficulties of the people.

Government Specially Approves Agricultural and Commercial Bank to Issue Agricultural Bonds; Methods to be Decided After Establishment; Total Amount Not to Exceed Fixed Capital

The New Sound Society reports that the Ministry of Industry is jointly organizing the Agricultural and Commercial Bank with various banks. The fixed capital and the loanable funds are both 30 million yuan. After the government allocates funds and the various banks approve them, the working capital will be handled by the various banks organizing an agricultural syndicate. The eleven official shareholders and directors have all been determined. The commercial shareholders and directors will be nominated at a meeting of the various banks this week and decided on the 8th. A reporter from the New Sound Society learned from banking circles yesterday that the bureau has been specially approved by the government to issue agricultural bonds. Furthermore, Article 10 of the regulations approved by the Executive Yuan states that "If necessary, the Agricultural and Commercial Bank may submit a request to the Ministry of Industry to forward to the government for approval to issue agricultural bonds, but the amount shall be limited to the total amount of the Agricultural and Commercial Bank's fixed capital. The issuance methods shall be decided by the Board of Directors after the establishment of the bureau." Furthermore, advanced countries such as France, Germany, Britain, the United States, and Japan have all issued agricultural bonds successively, which is an important way to raise agricultural funds. Because the amount of funds required for agriculture is too large and the term is too long, ordinary commercial banks cannot assume them. All banks in our country hope to realize this as soon as possible to adjust agricultural finance.

Zhejiang Finance Department Cables Reply to the All-Zhejiang Association

The All-Zhejiang Association in this city recently submitted a petition to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting a delay in the collection of the second installment of old taxes. The Finance Department has now replied by telegram: "To the Shanghai All-Zhejiang Association, your telegram has been noted with respect. Upon investigation, the Zhejiang Province's collection of arrears of taxes is limited to the period from December 1, 1935, to the day before the opening of the upper period of land tax in 1938, totaling more than two years. During this period, it is divided into five phases. We originally planned to use the method of phased repayment to allow the tax-owing households ample time to plan in advance. The first phase of collection in each county has been concluded. Now, starting from July 1, we are proceeding with the second phase of collection. In terms of taking into account the people's ability to pay, the department will instruct the counties to pay attention to this at any time. However, as it concerns the rectification of inherent tax revenues and the correction of the people's bad habits of owing grain, it is the established policy of this province and cannot be changed. We know that your association cares about local finances, and we hope you will give your full support so that Zhejiang Province's land tax can return to the normal practice of annual payment as soon as possible. We respectfully send this telegram in reply for your information. Cheng Yuanfan, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Finance Department, with seal."

Members of the Expedition to Examine Historical Sites in Shouxian Returned to Shanghai Yesterday; Said that Scientific Excavation is Necessary

Since a large number of bronzes were unearthed at the Lisanguidui in Zhujiaji, Shouxian, Anhui Province, on July 5, 1933, they have attracted the attention of scholars in China. However, because they were accidentally unearthed, the objects were soon scattered. Only more than 700 objects are currently preserved by the Anhui Provincial Library, which scholars regret. Last year, the Anhui Provincial Library, Anhui University, Shanghai Municipal Museum, Shanghai Municipal Library, Peking Library, Chinese Architecture Society, Archaeological Society, Oriental Culture Society, Jinling University, and the Chinese Cultural Research Institute jointly organized the Shouxian Historical Site Investigation Team, with Ye Gongchuo as the leader and Zheng Shixu as the secretary. At the beginning of this month, the team specially sent Shang Chengzuo, Hu Zhaochun, Zheng Shixu, and surveyor Li Changwen and chemical technician Cao Chunwei to conduct on-site survey work, which was completed yesterday and they returned to Shanghai. It is said that the Guidui has now been sealed off by the local government after excavation, and stagnant water and silt fill the ground. If scientific excavation is not carried out, it may be destroyed. Therefore, officials and gentry in Anqing and Shouxian are eager for the team to come to the county to cooperate. They provided the team with a lot of convenience for this survey, and the results of the work were very satisfactory.

Jiangsu Province Formulates Compound Fertilizers; Agricultural Sales Office Invests in Production; Sales to Begin at the Beginning of Next Month

Our country's farmland has been using chemical fertilizers for many years. The raw materials are all imported from countries such as Britain, Germany, the Netherlands, the United States, and Canada. The Jiangsu Provincial Government is concerned that the sale of mixed fertilizers may involve adulteration or insufficient content, which may harm crops or soil. Therefore, there are strict management measures. For example, the composition of the fertilizers is determined by the Construction Plant, which studies the nature of various crops and stipulates the minimum effective composition of various chemical fertilizer raw materials. Merchants must follow the formula. The provincial government has also established a reporting office in Shanghai. Merchants must report for approval and have the composition inspected to ensure compliance with the regulations before a license is issued, allowing them to sell and transport inland. The provincial government also dispatches many inspectors to various places to conduct random checks and guide farmers on how to apply and use the fertilizers. According to the investigation, the peak season for reporting the transport of chemical fertilizers is in July, August, and September. The sales area is mostly in Jiangnan. Now, most rice crops have switched to chemical fertilizers. From March of this year to recently, 8,000 bags of mixed fertilizers and 30,000 bags of ammonium sulfate have been reported for transport. This is because soybean cakes have risen in price this year, while chemical fertilizers have a fixed price, so farmers are happy to use them. Recently, Zhejiang Province has begun to formulate mixed fertilizers on its own, with the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank investing and acting as an agent. In Jiangsu Province, the Agricultural Product Sales Office will handle it. It purchased raw materials such as nitrogen phosphate and potassium chloride in Shanghai on the 27th to prepare 4,000 bags of mixed fertilizer, each weighing 100 kilograms (equivalent to 2 Shanghai dans), priced at 11 yuan and 75 cents, for sale starting at the beginning of next month.

Resumption of Work Yesterday Morning After the Municipal Party Department received the final reply from the workers, it immediately notified the factory to prepare for work. All male and female workers gathered at the factory gate at six o'clock yesterday morning. Dispute Regarding the labor-capital dispute, (1) the case of dismissing eleven workers, and (2) the request to improve treatment, the party and government organs have agreed on a mediation method, and will schedule another meeting to summon both labor and capital for mediation.

Report on Guizhou Drought Relief from Sino-Foreign Famine Relief Committee

The Sino-Foreign Famine Relief Committee at 97 Renji Road recently received a telegram from the Guizhou Branch reporting the drought and requesting relief. It is transcribed as follows: "[Omission of opening remarks] I, your subordinate, find that Guizhou Province has many mountains and little arable land, and the annual grain production is barely sufficient for self-sufficiency in normal times. Once a famine occurs, relief is difficult. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of summer this year, there has been a prolonged drought with no rain, and the scorching sun has burned the land, causing dry fields to be entirely unplanted. Most of the planted paddy fields are also facing the depletion of water sources, and the rice seedlings are withering day by day. As of now, a famine situation has already formed. Even if rain comes immediately, it will only save less than half of the crops. Moreover, the scorching sun continues day after day with no sign of rain. The people are panicking, and rice prices have suddenly increased many times over. The existing grain reserves among the people, even if distributed to the maximum extent, are estimated to last for only three months at most. If there is no harvest in the future, the tragic state of famine will be unbearable. This committee is in charge of disaster relief and should devise methods for prevention and rescue. However, in the face of a vast catastrophe, a large disaster area, and a severe disaster situation, no moment can be delayed. This committee's ability is limited, and its heart is more than its strength. We are compelled to appeal to all philanthropists at home and abroad to show great kindness and compassion, to provide spiritual guidance and material assistance. We are extremely grateful. In addition to submitting a separate report on the disaster situation, we are sending this telegram in advance." It is also heard that the committee has recently received reports from various districts in Anhui and Henan provinces that there has been no rain since the beginning of summer, and that epidemics are prevalent, with many cases of cholera in urban and rural areas. The infection is severe, and if methods are not devised for prevention and rescue, it will inevitably expand and spread. They are urgently hoping for large donations of summer medicine and epidemic prevention medicines, and earnestly hope that all sectors of society will provide as much assistance as possible, so that they can be transported to the disaster area to save lives and provide timely assistance, which would be the greatest virtue.

Xuzhou Disaster Relief Hospital Run by China International Famine Relief Commission to Close at the End of the Month

The China International Famine Relief Commission at 505 Henan Road, due to the prevalence of diseases among disaster victims in northern Jiangsu, specifically allocated funds to entrust the Christian Hospital and Kunwei Hospital of the Xuzhou Christian Presbyterian Church to operate a male and female disaster relief hospital respectively, providing diagnosis and medication to maintain the health of the suffering people. Male disaster victims suffering from illness were treated by the Christian Hospital, while women were treated by Kunwei Hospital. All medical expenses, including outpatient, house calls, and hospitalization, were borne by the Famine Relief Commission. From December of last year to the present, a total of 3,596 men and 2,918 women have been treated, and the total medical expenses have amounted to more than 8,000 yuan. The most common diseases are kala-azar, followed by anemia and nephritis. According to Doctor Gu Laiya, the causes of the diseases are nothing more than starvation and dampness. Now that the flood has receded and the number of patients is gradually decreasing, the Famine Relief Commission plans to close the disaster relief hospital this month.

Flour Exchange, Extraordinary General Meeting of Shareholders, Increase Capital by 250,000 Yuan

The Shanghai Flour Exchange, in order to increase share capital, convened an extraordinary general meeting of shareholders at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. 164 households attended, accounting for 8,905 shares (the company has a total of 316 households and 12,260 shares), which was sufficient for the legal quorum. Chairman Gu Xinyi first reported that shareholder Santai proposed to increase shares in order to consolidate the foundation and comply with the company law. Therefore, a meeting was specially convened to jointly study and discuss. As a result, (1) a resolution was passed to increase capital by 250,000 yuan to consolidate the foundation and maintain credibility. It was resolved that the capital be increased by 250,000 yuan, divided into 5,000 shares, each share being 50 yuan, to be fully paid at one time. Old shareholders are given priority, with each three old shares entitled to subscribe for one new share. If there are odd numbers, they will be calculated by dividing by four and taking six. Payment must be made in full within 20 days. If payment is not made by the deadline, the board of directors will raise funds separately. (2) A resolution was passed to increase the number of directors and supervisors, and a discussion will be held after the new shares are fully subscribed. (3) A resolution was passed to amend the company's articles of association, and a discussion will be held at the next annual general meeting of shareholders. (4) A resolution was passed to abolish the public warehouse, and the board of directors will solicit opinions from all parties and handle it at its discretion.

French Concession Tobacco Exchange Industry Opposes Sanitation Fee

The Fourth Branch of the Citizens' Federation sent a letter to the Taxpayers' Association, the Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens' Federation in the French Concession, regarding the French Municipal Council's levying of a categorized business sanitation fee on the tobacco exchange industry. The letter sent to the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association yesterday stated, "According to a joint letter from tobacco exchange shops such as Shengho Tai, Yanji, Peng Yongyuan, Dexinglong, Yikang, Ruichang, Chen Shengtai, Fuxingxiang, Hengtaixin, Jiufeng, Huitai, Hengsen, Hengyuan, Ruihe, Yongtai, Qiankangtai on Lafayette Road and Caishi Road, our shops have been operating in the French Concession for many years and have only paid patrol donations and tobacco exchange donations, and have never paid other taxes. Recently, the Categorized Business Office of the French Municipal Council suddenly sent Chinese and foreign personnel to inspect, claiming that because we also sell kerosene and candles, we must pay for a categorized business sanitation license, first paying an investigation fee of ten yuan, and we hear that we must also pay taxes on kerosene, etc., which is quite shocking. Our shops' concurrent sale of candles and kerosene is a necessary business for our industry, so the French authorities have never levied taxes in the past. At a time when the market is sluggish and the business of our industry is precarious, the French Municipal Council should try to reduce taxes so that merchants and residents can reduce their burdens in order to restore the prosperity. However, they disregard this and arbitrarily increase taxes, which is deeply incomprehensible to the Chinese taxpayers in the concession. Therefore, we jointly request that your association maintain commerce, allow us to propose negotiations, cancel the categorized business sanitation fee, in order to maintain our business and avoid public resentment," etc. In view of this, since the matter concerns the interests of Chinese taxpayers, it is reasonable to transfer the situation to your association for review and handling.

Midnight Joyride with Prostitute, Car Overturns into Ditch, Zhang Zhixiang's Extreme Joy Turns to Sorrow, Hongyu Laoqi Injured in Head and Face

Zhang Zhixiang, a 32-year-old from Wuxi, is currently working at the Gold Exchange. At 1:40 a.m. yesterday, Zhang and the prostitute Hongyu Laoqi from Fuzhili were riding in Zhang's car for a joyride in the countryside near Piyas Road in western Shanghai. However, the road there had no streetlights at night. The driver, Qian A'gen, saw a villager carrying vegetables on his shoulder to Shanghai for sale in the moonlight, so he swerved to the right to avoid him. As a result, the car overturned into a ditch on the side of the road due to the excessive speed. Zhang and Hongyu Laoqi were both cut on the head and face by glass. The driver, Qian A'gen, suffered a scraped right leg, but was fortunately not seriously injured. Later, they hired villagers to lift the car out of the ditch. It was estimated that only minor parts such as the front fender and glass were broken. As dawn was breaking, Zhang and others returned to Shanghai in the original car.

Page 11

Important Evidence in the Japanese Sailor Case: Pan Qiaoying Summoned for Testimony; Pu Provides Account of Seeing the Sailor and a Person in Western Clothing Walking; Identifies Faces of Ye Haisheng, etc., in Court, Saying She Does Not Recognize Them; In the Evening, Judge Xiao Goes to Avenue Doumer to Reenact the Scene

In the case of the Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo, who was shot and killed, after the First Special District Court declared the debate closed, the Shanghai Municipal Council, as the prosecutor, presented additional witnesses. Consequently, the presiding judge revoked the declaration of closure and resumed the process of examining evidence. Summonses were issued to witnesses, and a hearing was scheduled for the 31st of this month. The female witness, Pu Qiaoying, was located in Gaoyou, north of the Yangtze River, with the assistance of local authorities requested by the police department, who sent detectives there. She was brought to Shanghai the day before yesterday and taken to the First Special Court yesterday morning. The three defendants, Ye Haisheng, Yang Wendao, and Zhou Sherong, were escorted to the court. Judge Xiao XieFen presided over the hearing in the Third Tribunal. Prosecutor Zhang Zongru was also present to perform his duties. Mr. Ru Baoyi appeared as the lawyer for the police department. However, the defense lawyers for the defendants were not notified in time, except for Mr. Tang Huaiqun, who was at the court for another case and attended the Third Tribunal upon hearing about the witness examination. The others were absent. First, Mr. Ru stated the process of summoning Pu for testimony and declared that Pu had been interrogated by the police department after the incident, and her statement had already been submitted. Judge Xiao then examined the statement and questioned Pu Qiaoying, who testified that she was from Gaoyou. One afternoon around 7 or 8 PM, she was leading a child to play in Mindefang near the Japanese headquarters on the north side of North Sichuan Road, near Jiangwan Road. While passing Avenue Doumer, she saw a Japanese soldier proceeding north on the west side of Avenue Doumer, and another person in what appeared to be black Western clothing proceeding north on the east side. The soldier was ahead, and the person in Western clothing was behind. She was walking in the middle of the road, and the two were about two or three zhang apart. The court then ordered Pu to identify whether any of the three defendants, Ye, Yang, and Zhou, were the people she saw at the time. She said she did not recognize them. As she walked near a public stove, she suddenly heard a gunshot. She did not look back but entered the stove and took another route to return to her employer's house in Yonganli, telling her employer about the gunshot she heard on the way. However, she did not say who fired the shot, and she did not remember clearly, even though her employer asked. She then resumed her laundry work and was dismissed and returned to her hometown seven or eight days later. The court then asked if she could still recognize the places she had passed. She said she still remembered. The court then questioned the three defendants, asking if they had any objections to the witness's testimony. Ye and the others shook their heads. Judge Xiao then ordered Pu to leave, and the three defendants were returned to custody to await a rescheduled hearing.

Furthermore, after the court announced the rescheduling of the hearing yesterday, the court will not be in session on the 31st. However, the court believes it is necessary to have Pan Qiaoying (previously mistakenly written as Pu Qiaoying) reenact what she saw at the scene of the incident to clarify the facts. However, as the woman has recently married and must return to her hometown today, the court decided to go to Avenue Doumer again at 9 PM last night for a third on-site inspection, ordering Pan to reenact the scene in person. The matter was kept strictly confidential beforehand, so very few people knew about it. After this reporter learned of this news, I drove there at 9 PM. At 9:20 PM, Judge Xiao XieFen of the First Special Court, along with police lawyer Ru Baoyi and clerk Ding Zhongnan, arrived at the entrance of Avenue Doumer and Yonganli by car. Soon after, police detective Kelaote and Chinese detective Fan Defu arrived with Pan Qiaoying. Judge Xiao then ordered Pan to walk to Yili Store at No. 248, eleven storefronts from the end of North Sichuan Road to the north of Huanglu Road, next to the entrance of Defang (previously mistakenly written as Mindefang; the Tiantong'an train station is a few zhang north of this fang). After arriving at the entrance of the fang, she was ordered to reenact how she returned to No. 59 Yonganli that day, passing Avenue Doumer and witnessing the incident. Pan then crossed over from Mindefang to the opposite side of the road and walked along the roadside to the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Jiangwan Road. The judge then asked if she had seen any patrol officers when she walked to this point. She replied that she could not remember. She then turned into Avenue Doumer and walked south to No. 91. Pan said that she saw a Japanese soldier and a person in Western clothing coming towards her at this location. When she saw these two people, the Japanese soldier was standing at the entrance of No. 91 on the west side of Avenue Doumer, and the person in Western clothing was on the east side (opposite No. 90). Based on the calculation of crossing the road, the person in Western clothing was about two or three zhang away from the Japanese soldier. After seeing these two people, she continued south for about seventeen ordinary steps to the entrance of No. 191 (on the east side of Avenue Doumer, marked by the Chinese boundary). At that time, she heard the gunshot. She turned her head slightly (because Pan was carrying a three-year-old child on her back, she did not turn around). She saw the Japanese soldier had fallen to the ground. The judge then ordered clerk Ding to walk from the entrance of No. 91 to the place where the Japanese soldier fell to calculate the number of ordinary steps. After clerk Ding walked, he counted a total of nineteen ordinary steps. The judge then asked Pan if the streetlights were the same as today. She replied that they were not much different. He also asked if she saw a cobbler standing at the entrance of the Gaogang Laundry Shop. She replied that she did not remember clearly. He asked if she had seen a rickshaw parked. She replied that a rickshaw was parked at the entrance of Douleranli. The judge then ordered her to continue the reenactment. Pan then walked south from No. 191 into the Shunxingyuan public stove at No. 187 (also a Chinese boundary marker). From the back door of the public stove, she turned into Lane 3 of Yonganli and returned to No. 95, the home of her employer (because the entrance of the lane of Yonganli is at the end of North Sichuan Road and there is no lane entrance. If you want to go from Yonganli to Avenue Doumer, you must pass through the back door of each shop). The judge then ordered Pan to return to the scene of the incident. He ordered someone to wear a black suit found by the police in Hong Kong owned by Ye Haisheng. He asked Pan to look at it to see if the color of the suit was similar to the color of the clothing worn by the person in Western clothing she saw that day. She replied that the colors were similar and were also long pants and short jackets. He asked if the collar of the person in Western clothing was turned up that day. She replied that she did not remember clearly. At this point, a long time had passed, and all the points that needed to be investigated had been completed. Therefore, the investigation was declared complete. Xiao and Ding then drove back to the court. Because this investigation was decided on the spur of the moment, the defense lawyers for the defendants were not notified. The three defendants, Yang, Ye, and Zhou, were not brought along. Pan had been brought to this place by the police for a reenactment eight months ago. According to her, it was a little before 9 o'clock when she went from Mindefang to Avenue Doumer, because she knew it was 9 o'clock when she returned to her employer's house, so she was able to determine the time. The date of the trial of this case will be rescheduled, it is said.
