Relief Society: Donation of Disaster Relief Medicine

Since its establishment, the Guanyin Relief Society at the north entrance of Beile Road and Avenue Joffre in Shanghai has been enthusiastic in supporting public welfare and charitable causes. The society has now received a letter from the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Disaster Relief in Various Provinces, stating that last year, the victims of the floods in various provinces were indiscriminate in what they ate and drank, resulting in the rampant spread of epidemics since summer, and they were unable to seek medical treatment, and they died miserably. Recently, the number of people writing to the association to ask for medicine has increased day by day. It is known that Guanyin Relief Pills, supervised and manufactured by your society, are very effective in preventing and treating epidemics. A special letter is written to ask for a large amount of help so that it can be forwarded and achieve the same effect as saving all. The society first donated 2,000 boxes of Guanyin Relief Pills. Fearing that it would be a drop in the bucket and insufficient for distribution, it then solicited donations from philanthropists from all walks of life in order to raise a large amount of funds and seek universal relief. At present, 3,000 boxes of Guanyin Relief Pills and 2,800 bottles of Guanyin Relief Water have been raised and sent to the Disaster Relief Association for distribution. It is said that two more batches of disaster relief medicines will be sent in the next few days. In addition, the Buddhist hospital initiated by the society has established the first clinic in the society in order to provide relief for the sick and suffering. All monks are exempt from consultation fees and medicine costs, and ordinary people are charged a low registration fee for consultation and medicine. Therefore, the number of people going to seek treatment every day is quite crowded.

Rickshaw Industry: Affected by Registration; Many Cars Idle Due to Few Drivers

Since the public concessions and French concession in this city have successively conducted rickshaw puller registration, rickshaw merchants have been greatly affected by the business because there are many cars and few drivers. For example, the public concession limits the registration of 40,000 rickshaw pullers, but there are not as many rickshaw pullers actually pulling cars due to illness, death, or returning to their original hometowns north of the Yangtze River for various reasons. In addition, the French concession has suspended registration since the 10th of last month for more than a month. There are not a few people who have come to Shanghai from the countryside to prepare for registration and make a living by pulling carts, but they have returned to the countryside because they could not wait. Therefore, in the past, in hot weather like today, only 30-40% of the cars in each rickshaw line were idle. Now, the average number of cars on the street in the morning and evening shifts is less than half. Therefore, in the north and south cities and special districts, wherever there are more rickshaw lines, cars are connected and parked on the side of the road, which is full of them. However, the expenses of rent, donations, and labor are not reduced at all. Therefore, the price of cars has plummeted. Public concession cars (that is, cars with three-sided notices) are only more than 200 yuan per car, while those in the north and south cities are about 100 yuan. If this continues, the livelihood of hundreds of thousands of poor people will be extremely worrying. The authorities should quickly provide relief to avoid the rickshaw merchants and pullers from falling into a desperate situation.

No Discovery at the End of July: This Year's Cholera May Be Avoided; Seaport Quarantine Office Announces that the Rumor that Cholera Was Discovered in Ningbo Was a Misinformation

The Shanghai Seaport Quarantine Office of this city released the following information on the status of infectious diseases in the port of Shanghai last week: Three Chinese people contracted smallpox, and two died. Three Chinese people contracted epidemic meningitis. Twenty-nine Chinese people and eight foreigners contracted typhoid fever. Twenty-three Chinese people died. Nineteen Chinese people and three foreigners contracted bacterial dysentery and amoebic dysentery. Six Chinese people and one foreigner contracted diphtheria. One Chinese person died. Five Chinese people and three foreigners contracted scarlet fever. A total of sixty-five Chinese people and fifteen foreigners contracted infectious diseases, and twenty-six Chinese people died. According to Secretary Zhou Zhongqian, although it is the end of July, no true cholera has been discovered in Shanghai. All ports in the country are also very peaceful. As for the report that cholera was discovered in Ningbo, the Yinxian government has investigated and reported that it was misinformation. Therefore, this terrible cholera epidemic may be avoided this year.

On the morning of May 16, a car was driving along Yangshupu Road, and when it reached the end, it still did not realize it, causing it to drive into the Huangpu River. Seven people in the car died. The families of the deceased then filed a lawsuit against the Shanghai Municipal Council in the consular court, claiming that the facilities on the road were not properly equipped, causing this disaster, and demanding compensation for losses of 180,000 yuan. The lawyer of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Mr. Bolang, has filed a defense with the consular court, stating that the Shanghai Municipal Council cannot be held responsible for compensation in this case. The fault lies with the driver of the car for driving carelessly. The driver and the passengers knew that this road could lead to the new fish market. At that time, they were going there and should have turned into Dinghai Road and crossed the Dinghai Road Bridge, and should not have driven straight. The passengers knew that the driver had taken the wrong road, but they did not warn him, so they cannot be excused. Furthermore, this car belongs to the owner of a certain fish shop. On that day, the people took it to the fish market without the owner's permission, so it should be requested to cancel this case and order the plaintiff to pay the litigation costs. The date of the trial of this case has not yet been determined. It is said that it will be heard in September.

The Eighth Inspection Report of the Note Issuance Reserve Management Committee

The eighth inspection announcement of the Note Issuance Reserve Management Committee states: In accordance with Article 7 of the Committee's Articles of Association, the Committee inspected the legal tender reserves of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications on July 26, 1936. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of notes issued by the Central Bank is 300,871,929 yuan, and the total amount of reserves is 300,871,929 yuan, including 201,712,229 yuan in cash reserves and 99,159,700 yuan in guarantee reserves. (B) The total amount of notes issued by the Bank of China is 36,567,438.92 yuan, and the total amount of reserves is 36,567,438.92 yuan, including 23,272,347.18 yuan in cash reserves and 13,295,086.74 yuan in guarantee reserves. (C) The total amount of notes issued by the Bank of Communications is 21,040,095.51 yuan, and the total amount of reserves is 21,040,095.51 yuan, including 14,695,197.71 yuan in cash reserves and 6,345,897.80 yuan in guarantee reserves. The total amount of notes issued is 87,695,581.92 yuan, and the total amount of reserves is 87,695,581.92 yuan, including 58,138,767.18 yuan in cash reserves and 29,556,814.74 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above amounts of note issuance and reserves show that the cash reserves exceed 60% and the guarantee reserves are below 40%, which is in compliance with the Committee's inspection rules. This is hereby announced.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 293rd Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: This Committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued and the reserves of this Bank in accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law. The 293rd inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this Bank on July 25, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 300,871,929 silver yuan, including 269,273,392 silver yuan notes and 31,592,537 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 300,871,929 silver yuan, including 201,712,229 silver yuan in cash reserves. These cash reserves include 106,134,906.79 yuan deposited in the Bank's issuance branches and sub-branches and 95,577,322.21 yuan deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 99,159,700 silver yuan. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 400,963.07 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserves is 400,963.07 yuan. This reserve includes 7,926.290 ounces of pure gold, valued at 51.68 customs gold per ounce, totaling 400,963.07 yuan. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder is guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is hereby reported. July 27, 1936, Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Chairman Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

Jin Tongyin Grieves Over the Loss of His Son

Jin Xiansun, the eldest son of Jin Qiansun, a respected elder from Jiaxing, was only in his early twenties. He was excellent in character and academics, having studied at Fudan University, Datong University, and the School of Political Science and Law, always excelling among his peers and earning the praise of his teachers. However, his body was weak, and he studied diligently, which led to him contracting lumbar tuberculosis. He received multiple treatments from his uncle, Dr. Jin Wenqi, and other renowned Chinese and Western doctors, but it would recover and then relapse, never being completely cured. In the past month, his condition suddenly worsened, affecting his lungs, stomach, and other organs, and he passed away at 7 PM on July 26th, at the young age of 21. Yesterday, the coffin was placed at the China Funeral Home on Hart Road. It is said that it will be temporarily stored for a few months before being transported back to his hometown for burial. The Jin family has many friends, but due to the loss of a young family member, few announcements were made. However, friends and relatives who came to express their condolences yesterday morning were endless, all lamenting his loss, it is said.

Minhang Ferry Manager Zhan Weizeng is Indicted for Negligence Resulting in Death; Investigation Clarifies the Facts

Yang Bingsheng, the sixteen-year-old son of Yang Dianchen, a policeman at the First Branch Bureau of the County Public Security Bureau stationed in Minhang Town, was an apprentice at the Feilong Motor Shop on Jiuguo Road in the town. On the evening of the 11th of this month at around 9 PM, he went to the railing of the Minhang Ferry Terminal of the Highway Administration Office of the Construction Department to cool off due to the hot weather. He soon fell asleep. Unexpectedly, he was kicked by Zhan Weizeng, the ferry manager, and injured, causing him to fall into the river and drown. After the deceased's father, Yang Dianchen, reported the incident to the local court, Prosecutor Xiao Jinying arrived at the scene to examine the body. Zhan was summoned for questioning and released on bail pending further investigation. Zhan Weizeng also accused Yang Dianchen of assault. It is now known that Prosecutor Xiao has indicted Zhan Weizeng for negligence resulting in death. The facts of the crime are as follows: Yang Bingsheng, the son of Yang Dianchen, was sleeping on the shore of the Minhang Ferry Terminal on the night of the 11th of this month because of the heat. Zhan Weizeng, the ferry manager, kicked Yang Bingsheng under his right eyelid because he should not have been sleeping on the dock. When Yang Bingsheng woke up in fright, he could not discern the direction and was also blinded by Zhan Weizeng's flashlight, causing him to lose his footing and fall into the river and drown. Afterwards, Yang Dianchen negotiated with Zhan Weizeng and was assaulted by him. (Evidence and relevant legal provisions) Yang Bingsheng died of drowning after being injured while alive, which has been verified. The injury was inflicted by the defendant. Li Afu and Zheng Buyun, who were sleeping with Yang Bingsheng at the time, witnessed the incident. Li Afu was also awakened by the defendant's kick at the same time, and his testimony is highly credible. Yang Bingsheng drowned because he was kicked awake from a deep sleep, causing him to lose his senses and lose his footing. This has also been confirmed by Li Afu and others. Therefore, Yang Bingsheng's death was caused by the defendant's negligence, which is beyond doubt. The defendant's assault on Yang Bingsheng and Yang Dianchen, and negligence resulting in Yang Bingsheng's death, constitute offenses under Article 277, Paragraph 1 and Article 276, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and should be prosecuted according to the law. A public trial will be held soon. As for Zhan Weizeng's accusation against Yang Dianchen for assault, the prosecution was dropped. The reason given was that the defendant's son, Yang Bingsheng, was negligently killed by Zhan Weizeng. The defendant negotiated with Zhan Weizeng, and they fought. The defendant inflicted a minor injury on Zhan Weizeng's left elbow. However, considering the defendant's motive for committing the crime was that his son was kicked and drowned by Zhan Weizeng, his situation is extremely pitiful and should be dismissed in accordance with Article 232 of the Criminal Procedure Law.

The Assassination Case in Lujiazhai, Pudong, the Night Before Last; The Deceased, Zhang Xiaobei, Had a Previous Criminal Record

At 11 PM the night before last, an assassination case occurred on the Land Temple Road in Lujiazhai, Pudong. A young man wearing a white twill short-sleeved shirt and trousers was shot and killed while passing by. After the incident, the local police station found that the deceased's name was Zhang Xiaodi, 21 years old, a local resident living at No. 52 Wufu Lane, Lujiazui Road. His father, Zhang Liuting, was notified. Yesterday morning, the local guarantor, Lu Shunlong, was instructed to report the case to the local court for an inquest. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Deng Peiyi, accompanied by Examiner Shen Qixiu, crossed the river to the scene and verified that the bullet entered from the back of the head and exited through the left eye socket, confirming that the death was caused by a gunshot wound. The death certificate was completed, and the family was allowed to collect the body pending investigation of the killer. It is said that the deceased had previously committed a crime and was sentenced to one year in prison by the First Special District Court. He was released after serving his term, which was less than half a year ago.

The Egg Industry of Shanghai (Continued) (An Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, Part 33)

— Compiled by China Credit Information

(6) Business Conditions

In the Shanghai egg business, frozen eggs are directly exported by the factories, while egg products are handled by export firms. In the past, when selling to foreign merchants, there was a guarantee that the goods would not spoil for four months. This led to some cunning foreign merchants being overly critical, arbitrarily returning goods. Moreover, with the instability of foreign exchange rates, foreign merchants would adjust their acceptance and return of goods based on the rise and fall of the pound sterling. Many egg merchants went bankrupt as a result. Later, after public discussion, the bad practice of guaranteeing goods was abolished, eliminating losses in sales. Last year, the government reformed the currency system, and egg merchants had more security due to the stability of foreign exchange.

Regarding the future of the business, based on our institute's investigation, we are optimistic. First, the government is supporting the egg industry, such as reducing tax rates and guiding improvements. Officials and merchants can cooperate well. Second, any egg products from our country are of excellent quality, and foreign merchants cannot find any flaws. Third, industry leaders such as Mr. Zheng Yuanxing have visited Europe and America several times to investigate the production and sales of eggs, and are familiar with the situation. Knowing the enemy and oneself makes it easier to control the situation. Fourth, the industry has realized that competition is not a good strategy, and are cooperating sincerely with each other. Even foreign egg factories have established new names and joined the Shanghai Egg Industry Association. As for the embargo on Chinese eggs by various countries, our government authorities have, together with egg merchants, been actively seeking countermeasures. With these factors, the fate of the egg industry will not follow the path of silk and tea.

(7) Market Price of Eggs

Egg prices depend entirely on supply and demand. Secondly, the seasons also have an impact. Generally, prices rise in winter and fall in summer. Frozen eggs are directly exported, so there is no market price in Shanghai. The following is a comparison of Shanghai egg prices in the past year, to get a glimpse of the trend: Monthly Price Chart of Fresh Eggs (Unit: 100 Jin, Yuan)

(8) Analysis of the Shanghai Egg Industry

The Shanghai egg industry can be divided into four categories: egg factories, traditional egg factories, export firms, and egg shops. Among them, egg shops have the longest history. The Chengyutang Public Office was the old-time group of this industry. Later, it joined with egg factories to form the Shanghai Egg Industry Association. The association is located at 1127 Shanshou Lane, Broadway Road, with more than 30 members. Traditional egg factories also have an Egg Factory Association, located at 19, Lane 145, Tianjin Road. It is said that the two associations are planning to merge for the sake of unity. The following is a detailed description of each category:

There are currently six frozen egg factories, five foreign-owned and one Chinese-owned. Each factory has strong capital, and some also operate various animal products. Banta has the oldest qualifications and specializes in egg products. Jardine Matheson and Bering, British merchants, have factories in Shanghai and branches in Qingdao. Maocheng Company, a Chinese merchant, is the only frozen egg factory in China today. The head office is located at 229 Huangpu Road, Shanghai, and the branch is located at 4 Shanghe Road, Qingdao. The internal organization is divided into the purchasing department, factory affairs department, export department, and transportation department. It also has a cold storage department and a branch in London, with agents in various countries. Due to sufficient resources, outstanding talent, and excellent credit, it has achieved its current position.

Summer Chinese Clothing

— Rong Yu

The best conditions for clothes worn in summer are "comfort," "simplicity," and "lightness." Our domestic fabrics and tailoring styles happen to meet these standards. No wonder Westerners living in Shanghai are also changing to Chinese clothing and swaggering along the road with Western steps (see the previous Japanese newspaper). Indeed! Domestic fabrics, such as spun silk, Xiangyun yarn, and summer cloth, are light, thin, and durable, and do not stick to sweat. Moreover, Chinese clothing styles are loose, cool, and extremely comfortable. They are also very convenient to put on and take off, and the price is cheap. A gown for about ten yuan and a set of shirt and trousers for about ten yuan are already top-quality goods. Even washing is very simple. A clever servant in the home can wash them clean and iron them neatly. On the other hand, wearing a suit is not so comfortable and economical. The fabric of suits is always white drill or white canvas, which is thick and worn on the body, providing no coolness at all. Moreover, the waist of the trousers is the same size as the body, plus the pockets, it is almost like a pair of lined trousers in Chinese clothing. Do you think it is hot to wear? The thin shirt on the upper body, although said to be loose and comfortable, but you cannot just wear a shirt in formal occasions. Adding a tie or bow tie, and then wearing a thick coat, it is really terribly hot. Moreover, a basic suit costs about twenty yuan; plus, not everyone can wash it, taking it to a laundry shop also costs several dimes. Think about spending so much money to get uncomfortable, what's the point! So, in the summer, I advise those who wear Chinese clothing not to be envious and learn to wear suits; even those who wear suits may as well switch to domestic Chinese clothing, and compare which is more comfortable and convenient.

However, Chinese clothing also has some inconveniences. The gown is really too long, making it inconvenient to get on and off vehicles, walk, and work. General Ma Zizhen once advocated shortening the length of the gown to the knees, which is truly convenient and beautiful.

Contributing Words: The Domestic Goods Industry Should Take the Lead in Using Domestic Goods

— Yang Fei

I often say that to promote domestic goods, it is better to rely on ourselves than on others, and it is better to persuade people within the domestic goods industry than those outside it. In particular, those of us who serve the domestic goods industry should take the lead in practicing what we preach. This is more effective and easier to promote.

First method: The domestic goods industry should organize a large group. Everyone who serves the domestic goods industry must purchase and use domestic goods, and must purchase and use domestic goods produced by the factories of this group. Anyone who purchases and uses domestic goods produced by the group's factories is entitled to preferential prices or discounts.

Second method: All comrades who serve the domestic goods industry must swear to use domestic goods. The whole family, old and young, male and female, must use domestic goods. If it is found that non-domestic goods are purchased, the factory or store leader should impose the most severe punishment, or even dismiss or fire the employee.

Third method: All interpersonal interactions, congratulatory gifts, and condolences of people who serve the domestic goods industry should use domestic goods gift certificates. Anyone who holds domestic goods gift certificates to purchase goods at domestic goods companies or factories should be given special treatment.

Fourth method: Domestic goods factories should introduce their products to each other, so that colleagues in each factory have the habit of purchasing and using domestic goods. At the same time, factories should sign contracts with each other, setting preferential terms, so that each can obtain goods at favorable prices.

Fifth method: Each factory or company should organize a cooperative, and the clothing, food, housing, and transportation of all members should be based on the principle of using domestic goods. Later, bonuses will be determined based on the amount of domestic goods purchased.

This work of the domestic goods industry itself is also the basic work of promoting domestic goods, and in fact, it is the minimum work of using domestic goods. If this point can be implemented, there is still bright hope for the future of domestic goods. Otherwise, empty talk will not help in practice, and the word "promotion" is still equivalent to nonsense.

Promoting Domestic Goods and Revitalizing Rural Areas

— Tang Zenggeng

Our country is known as an agricultural country, and farmers account for the vast majority of the population. Since the misfortune of rural bankruptcy, the countryside has been in a state of death. On the one hand, this is indeed due to the adversity of natural and man-made disasters, which has made the countryside an irreparable situation. On the other hand, we cannot but say that the giant claws of imperialist economic aggression have stretched into the countryside, causing it to be covered in endless gray. Therefore, the countryside has been in a long-term decline, and farmers have suffered permanent pain. The saying that we are an agricultural country may be fundamentally shaken?

Here, let us temporarily set aside the first reason for rural bankruptcy—natural and man-made disasters—because this is not within the scope of this article. Now, let us talk about the second reason for rural bankruptcy caused by imperialist economic aggression.

It is undeniable that the economic aggression of imperialists has brought misfortune to every member of China. They use Chinese raw materials to manufacture goods, and then sell them back to China. In this process, the invaders' pockets are filled, while China's money flows out. How can the country's wealth not cause extreme panic? How can the rural economy not feel infinite distress? Therefore, if we want to revitalize the countryside, we must start with promoting domestic goods.

To make domestic goods penetrate into rural areas, to enable rural areas to be revitalized, and to eliminate the traces of imperialist economic aggression in rural areas, I think we should pay attention to the following points:

1. Promoting the domestic goods manufacturing industry can revitalize the rural economy: To make domestic goods penetrate into rural areas, we should strive to promote the domestic goods manufacturing industry to go to rural areas, so that every idle farmer can obtain a means of livelihood, and the rural economy can gradually improve. This requires the government authorities to increase their supervision and encouragement, and establish more domestic goods manufacturing factories, so that rural areas can restore their vitality.

2. Establishing domestic goods service agencies to make farmers happy to use domestic goods: We admit that the belief in foreign goods has now deeply influenced the minds of farmers. They consider using foreign goods to be the supreme glory. This can be said to be a major problem of rural bankruptcy. Therefore, now that we want to revitalize the countryside, we hope that people from all walks of life will work together to establish domestic goods service agencies, and try their best to introduce domestic goods to rural areas and to farmers, and also have to make efforts to persuade them to be happy to use domestic goods, and to eradicate the psychology of believing in foreign goods.

3. Establishing domestic goods training institutes to enable farmers to acquire knowledge of domestic goods:

For this item, we need teachers engaged in rural education to do some work. Please ask them to join several schools and establish a domestic goods training institute, and invite farmers to listen to lectures to impart to them very simple knowledge of domestic goods. We do not seek profundity, but only popularity, so that they can understand the main cause of rural bankruptcy, and so that they know the knowledge of using domestic goods. With such earnest persuasion, farmers' knowledge of domestic goods will gradually increase and they will reject foreign goods.

Although the relief of rural bankruptcy cannot be achieved solely by the above three points, it can at least provide some assistance under the general mobilization to revitalize the countryside. Here, I deeply hope that government authorities, people from all walks of life, and the teachers and ladies who are responsible for relieving the countryside, will work hard to reverse the misfortune of rural bankruptcy and step up our rural revitalization.

A Record of Mr. Tan Yutian, Inventor of Radio-Controlled Boats

— Cun

Tan Yutian of Nanjing is a handsome young man, only about 30 years old this year. Originally from Guangdong, he has lived in the Northeast for many years, studying electrical machinery for seven or eight years. He is the author of various books on radio principles, repair methods, design methods, circuit diagrams, and double heterodyne design methods. He witnessed the heartbreaking scenes of the Northeast's fall, so he worked hard to study, in order to contribute to the country in the future.

His motivation for experimenting with radio-controlled boats began three years ago. He only started manufacturing in August or September of last year, creating a small radio-controlled boat that is three and five-tenths feet long, displaces one cubic meter, and has a payload of 62 pounds. In addition to the motor, the boat is equipped with a receiver, controller, etc. During the test, a transmitter with a wavelength of 74 meters was installed on the shore. By pressing the components, the electric boat can be induced to move freely left, right, forward, and backward. In the future, after expansion, it can also be equipped with guns, smoke screens, searchlights, and other components to complete a perfect electric warship.

Due to economic reasons, Mr. Tan spent 400 yuan to build this small electric boat. When he tested it at Xuanwu Lake in the capital a few days ago, Mr. Tan stood on the shore and turned the transmitter. The electric boat gradually left the shore. If he wanted it to go east, it would go east. If he wanted it to go backwards, it would go backwards. His preliminary research has been completed with satisfaction.

Now, Mr. Tan is preparing to carry out his second major plan. He hopes to cooperate with the Ministry of Transportation and other agencies, and hopes that the government will provide material and spiritual assistance to fulfill his wishes. In addition, he is also researching an ultra-shortwave motor of one meter to five meters, which can be carried around and communicate with a few miles away. It is said that it will be successful in half a year.

Cheng Tianfang, the country's ambassador, and all the athletes of the delegation were invited to participate. Inside the venue, the national flags of China and Germany and the flag of the Olympic Games were hung, which was extremely beautiful. Dr. Wang Zhengting gave a speech, saying that after the closing of the conference, the athletes of the Chinese team would often travel to various parts of Germany to broaden their horizons. Ambassador Cheng Tianfang gave a speech, saying that the Olympic Games is a bridge connecting the civilizations of China and Germany. Finally, President Dai Jitao gave a speech, saying that Sun Zhongyou's last words said that the construction of a new China should be based on the three virtues of prudence, fraternity, and courage. The Chinese nation is eager to study the process of Germany's recovery after the war. In addition to the dinner, the welcome party also performed various recreational programs, such as music, martial arts, and drama, to add to the fun. German guests especially appreciated it.

Record of the World Games Team's Accompanying Journey (Letter No. 4) Central News Agency Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen

The flag of the British Empire, where the sun always shines, is truly felt to be great when we step out of our country's borders. Since leaving Shanghai, we have passed through Hong Kong and Singapore, all of which are its colonies. Now, we have arrived in Colombo, the capital of Ceylon Island, and soon we will go to Bombay in India. These places are all British territories. The maritime route between Europe and Asia is almost entirely encompassed by it. Britain, based on a mere three islands, has achieved such great development. This makes the people of our ancient nation feel only shame and nowhere to hide.

Ceylon Island is located at the southern tip of India and is a territory directly under British administration. Colombo is the capital of Ceylon Island and the center of the Indian Ocean sea route, as well as the first important port on the Indian Ocean coast. The British have established a governor to govern Ceylon Island, and the governor resides in Colombo. The mail ship arrived in Colombo at noon on July 4th. Colombo faces the Indian Ocean. To prevent waves from impacting and to avoid wind and waves, the Ceylon government has built two stone dikes in the ocean, surrounding a small bay. The construction of the stone dikes is very majestic and grand. Outside the stone dikes, turbulent waves crash, creating water splashes more than ten feet high, falling like a fountain in bursts. Although we are already tired of sea travel, we only find such scenery magnificent and lovely. Inside the stone dikes, the water is clear and calm, with many giant ships and warships anchored.

The mail ship docked in the bay at noon. Due to passport checks, it was not until 2 PM that we began to disembark. The distance from the docking point to the shore is several hundred meters. The mail ship company prepared a small ferry to pick up passengers. Many people missed this ferry and had to take a commercial ferry, which cost one rupee (the Ceylon currency, equivalent to one yuan and three jiao in the national currency). They all exclaimed that they were very unlucky.

There are not many overseas Chinese in Colombo. The pier was deserted, and no one came to welcome us, so after going ashore, everyone acted freely. The mail ship was scheduled to set sail at 8 PM, giving us plenty of time to tour the city. Many owners of automobile businesses came to solicit business, offering three-hour tours of the city for one pound per car (six people per car). So everyone split up and set off in groups. There were also many thrifty friends who simply strolled around the nearby streets and browsed the shops.

The reporter, along with Chu Anping from the Central Daily News, and Wu Demao, Shao Rugan, Jiang Lianggui, and Hou Luoxun from the inspection team, rode in one car. We first went to the telegraph office to send a telegram. After sending the telegram, the chauffeur drove to the gas station to refuel. When the car stopped, many dark-skinned locals came to give us a few flowers. We gave them ten cents, but they still complained. This kind of disguised beggar is everywhere. If you walk on the street, you will be entangled by them endlessly.

The car drove around the city for three hours. We could not even call it a fleeting glimpse. Now, I will just say a little about the surface situation of Colombo to give those who have not been there a simple outline.

The roads in Colombo are also flat and wide. Perhaps in all imperialist colonies, this little bit of material civilization can always be enjoyed. Many tall foreign firms stand tall, forming a modern city. However, the houses of the locals are small and dirty, not harmonious or commensurate at all. The most lovely thing is the many tall trees, lush and shady, everywhere like a garden.

The means of transportation on the street, besides a few cars and rickshaws, are still mainly bullock carts. The structure of the bullock carts is very heavy, with a wooden board sandwiched between two iron giant wheels. A semi-circular awning made of sugarcane mat is built on top, even taller than a small house. Depending on the size and weight of the cart, one or two oxen are used to pull it. They walk slowly and continuously on the street, not only making the streets very crowded, but also leaving cow dung everywhere, which is extremely smelly. Especially in the small streets, it is nauseating.

The crows in Colombo can probably be considered the boldest of their kind. They are everywhere in the streets and open spaces. They are certainly not afraid of people. Even when cars rush by, they simply take a few steps and give way, just like those veteran road inspectors, and do not spread their wings and fly high. Everyone, seeing this situation, said with a smile that Colombo can be called the world of crows.

Colombo does not have anything particularly admirable or memorable. We acted as road inspectors for three hours and only stopped at two places. The first was Victoria Park. The entire park is very large, with lush trees and flourishing flowers and plants. The scenery is very quiet. The city hall next to the park is one of the most magnificent buildings in the city. The boundaries between the white people and the locals' recreational areas in the park are very strict. The area nearby is mostly the residence of white people. When the chauffeur explained this to us, he showed a very envious expression. The second place we stopped was the Shakyamuni Temple. People who go to the temple must take off their shoes. We also followed suit at the entrance. A temple attendant (actually a guide) accompanied us inside. The temple is octagonal in shape and not very large. There is a corridor all around, and the middle is the Buddha hall. In the Buddha hall, there is a statue of a large Buddha and several small Buddhas. The walls are painted with many pictures about Buddhist stories, some with modern decorations. Everyone laughed and said that the Bodhisattva has also become modernized. To the west of the Buddha hall, there are also several side rooms. One room has a marble statue of Guanyin, which is very exquisite. In the corridor, there is also a reclining Buddha more than two feet long, which can be called magnificent. The difference between this temple and Chinese temples is that there are no incense candles inside, and it is exceptionally clean, not at all like the messy appearance of Chinese halls. When we were in the Buddha hall, the guide gave each person a fresh flower, saying that it could bring good luck. Everyone, of course, smiled it off. When leaving the temple, he asked us for money. Many people gave him one yuan, and some gave a few jiao. When putting on shoes, many locals competed to help you put them on, and of course, they could not do without money. In the eyes of the locals, there is nothing more important than money.

The "Curry" chicken in India and Ceylon is very famous. Everyone was tired of eating the big mountain rice on the ship and went to try something different. A plate of rice with a piece of chicken costs one rupee, but there is no "Curry." Another plate of "Curry" chicken is another half a rupee. The taste is not particularly unique. It was really a small deception.

Ceylon is famous for producing pearls, gems, tea, and graphite. The chauffeur drove us to a jewelry store. Although the storefront was not very large, it displayed many pearls and gems, which were truly dazzling and beautiful. The shop assistants were very attentive, taking this and that to show you, and saying how fair the prices were, and that you could earn several times the interest in Europe. However, none of us wanted to be jewelers, so we only bought a few landscape postcards to get it over with.

The brown-skinned Ceylonese locals have dark, shiny skin. Because they like to eat betel nuts, their lips are dyed bright red, like basins of blood. Poor locals do not wear clothes on their upper bodies, and their lower bodies are wrapped in a piece of cloth instead of pants. Both men and women are bareheaded and barefoot. However, students are neatly dressed in shoes and socks, showing that this nation is also making progress to some extent. Locals carry goods, except for the heaviest ones using bullock carts, and the rest are carried on their heads. We often see many men and women on the street, carrying a very tall bag on their heads, walking lightly, without showing any signs of effort. (To be continued)

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders Issuance of Standards for Hygiene Facilities in Colleges and Above

The Ministry of Education issued an order on the 27th to all public and private colleges and universities across the country, stating, "Having investigated the temporary standards for hygiene facilities in colleges and above, which have been formulated by this Ministry, in addition to announcing and distributing them, the temporary standards are hereby issued, instructing the schools to comply with them."

Temporary Standards for Hygiene Facilities in Colleges and Above

I. Objectives: (1) To strengthen hygiene facilities in colleges and universities, providing appropriate diagnosis, treatment, and prevention of diseases for all faculty, staff, students, and workers. (2) To improve environmental hygiene within the school to ensure safety of life and promote individual health. (3) To cultivate students' correct concepts of hygiene, so that they can take on the responsibility of guiding society and promoting national health.

II. Organization: (1) Colleges and universities should establish a fixed organization responsible for handling school hygiene, such as a Health Section, Health Group, or Hygiene Section, Hygiene Group, etc. (2) Colleges and universities should jointly organize a School Hygiene Committee, or a committee of equivalent significance, with various related departments within the school to design school hygiene matters. (3) If colleges and universities have departments of health education or health education, school hygiene matters should be handled by those departments.

III. Personnel: School hygiene directors in colleges and universities should be staffed by health education or medical professionals. In addition to the director, full-time physicians, nurses, pharmacists, etc. should be hired as appropriate, and, to the extent possible, hygiene inspectors, dentists, and assistants should be added.

IV. Funding: The funding for school hygiene programs in colleges and universities should account for approximately 2% of the total school budget each year. This funding should be included in the annual budget.

V. Key Work Items: (1) Health Examination: New students must pass a health examination to be admitted. Old students should undergo a review examination once at the beginning of each academic year. Students in poor health may be examined by the health section physician at any time if deemed necessary. (2) Environmental Hygiene: (a) Management of janitors and kitchen workers. (b) Inspection and maintenance of environmental hygiene on campus. (c) Implementation of hygiene regulations. (d) Environmental hygiene design and improvement of the entire school. (3) Vaccination: New students must undergo vaccination for cowpox, typhoid fever and cholera. (4) Management of Infectious Diseases: When a statutory infectious disease is discovered in the school, in addition to strictly isolating the patient and providing appropriate treatment, the local health authorities must be notified immediately. (5) Diagnosis and Treatment of Diseases: Daily treatment clinics and weekly diagnostic clinics should be held. (6) Health Academic Lectures: Experts should be hired to give lectures on health knowledge outside of class. (7) Conduct training classes for hygiene workers, organized by health personnel.

VI. Equipment: (1) Furniture, equipment, and medicines used for diagnosing and treating diseases. (2) Health records (records of health examinations, correction of deficiencies, and diagnosis and treatment of diseases). (3) Microscopes and equipment for examining sputum, feces, and blood cells and hemoglobin. (4) Dormitories with more than 200 students should have a convalescent room with two beds and necessary convalescent equipment. (5) Equipment for disposing of garbage and exterminating mosquitoes and flies, and forms for inspecting environmental hygiene. (6) Equipment for vaccination. (7) Weight and height measuring instruments. (8) Various health education charts and books.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Stipulates Salaries for Primary School Principals and Teachers

(Zhenjiang News) The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an instruction to the education bureaus of various counties yesterday, stating, "Upon investigating the salary standards for primary school principals in various counties, they are generally determined based on the amount of local education funds. As a result, the amounts are uneven and the differences are too great. In poor counties, the monthly income of primary school teachers is often insufficient to provide for their own basic needs, which is highly inappropriate. At the same time, although the principle of paying salaries based on qualifications is the same, the distinctions in qualifications are also uneven. This Department has long been determined to adjust this situation, but because the sources of education funds in various counties cannot be increased with the current resources, and the differences are very large, a comprehensive plan must be carefully decided to avoid excessive favoritism or bias, which would further increase difficulties. Now, we have received an instruction from the Ministry of Education, ordering us to immediately plan methods to increase the salaries of primary school teachers. At the same time, the 24th year has ended, and the 25th year's education budget for each county is being finalized. Therefore, the adjustment measures should be promptly drafted and promulgated. Therefore, based on the current situation of each county, we have formulated 17 articles of the Temporary Measures for Salary Standards of County-Level Primary School Principals and Teachers in Jiangsu Province. In addition to issuing separate orders, we are also issuing them for the information of the county. Please promptly revise or draft your county's own measures in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the said measures and submit them for approval and implementation. Urgently."

Standards for Salaries of County-Level Primary School Principals and Teachers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province

I. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has formulated these measures in order to implement the Ministry's order to increase the salaries of primary school teachers, adjust the salary standards of primary school principals and teachers in various counties, and improve educational efficiency. II. The qualifications of primary school principals and teachers are divided into the following five grades: Grade A: Graduates of normal universities, university education colleges, education departments, higher normal schools, and vocational normal schools. Grade B: Graduates of old-system normal undergraduate programs, high school normal programs, and special normal programs. Grade C: Graduates of provincial rural normal schools and those who have passed non-examination qualifications. Grade D: Graduates of provincial and county-level teacher training classes and those who have passed examination qualifications. Grade E: Those who meet the qualifications of substitute teachers under primary school regulations. III. Monthly salaries of primary school teachers must be determined according to the qualification grades in the preceding paragraph, with a difference of two to four yuan between each grade. However, the starting salary grade for each grade of teacher must comply with the following provisions: Grade A qualification: Starting salary of at least 20 yuan. Grade B qualification: Starting salary of at least 18 yuan. Grade C qualification: Starting salary of at least 16 yuan. Grade D qualification: Starting salary of at least 14 yuan. Grade E qualification: Starting salary of at least 12 yuan. IV. Full-time teachers of primary schools who concurrently serve as principals of two grades or less should be promoted one grade at the start of their salary, and those serving as principals of three or more grades should be promoted one and a half grades. V. Full-time teachers of senior primary schools should be promoted one grade at the start of their salary. Those who concurrently serve as principals of two-grade complete primary schools should be promoted two grades, and those serving as principals of four or more grades should be promoted three grades. VI. Elementary primary schools should be based on a first-grade teacher. If the number of students exceeds 35, they can be promoted one grade for every 10 additional students. If there are more than five, they can also be promoted by half a grade. If there are three or more grades, and the average number of students per grade reaches 50, one additional subject teacher may be added. However, full-time teachers will not be promoted, and subject teachers should be paid at the lowest grade. VII. Senior primary schools should be based on two grades, two full-time teachers, and one subject teacher. If the number of students in each grade reaches 40, full-time teachers may be promoted one grade, and subject teachers may be promoted half a grade. For every five additional students above 40, they should be promoted once according to the proportion. This calculation applies to schools with three or only one grade of senior primary school. VIII. If the number of students in each grade of senior primary school is less than 30, the full-time teacher's salary will be reduced by one grade. If the number of students is less than 25, the school will be closed or merged. If the number of students in each grade of elementary primary school is less than 35, the full-time teacher's salary will be reduced by one grade. If the number of students is less than 30, the school will be closed or merged. IX. Teachers who are promoted due to an increase in students may be demoted at any time according to the reduced number of students. X. The number of students stipulated in the above articles may be appropriately increased or decreased by each county after approval from the provincial government, based on local conditions. XI. Principals and teachers who work diligently and achieve excellent results and are commended or praised by provincial and county superintendents may be promoted one or two grades. Those who continue to strive for excellence may be promoted again. However, those who make progress backwards may also be demoted at any time. XII. Those in each county who have already been given a labor bonus may be promoted by several grades, maintaining their original treatment, but they should still be subject to promotion and demotion at any time in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article. XIII. Schools should submit the resumes and supporting documents of the teachers they intend to hire to the education bureau or the third section of the county government for approval of the starting salary grade within one month before the start of each semester. If the qualifications are not met, the section may order the school to hire another teacher or directly appoint one. XIV. Each section should conduct a teacher registration once every two months before the start of each semester. When teachers with qualifications in the A, B, C, and D categories who have already registered cannot all be hired, teachers with E qualifications may not be hired. XV. The number of students at each level should be calculated on the average number of students seen by school inspectors. However, children under the age of six and students who have completed their study years should be excluded. XVI. For expenses standards in all grades of schools where the standards are calculated based on school level or that do not have defined treatment grades, and where the conditions set for pay standards do not meet the standards set in these regulations, a plan for standards should be set separately and submitted for approval and implementation. If the original grade expense budget for each grade exceeds the minimum standards set in these measures, the starting pay grade should be appropriately raised, but should not exceed the original budget scope. For school grades that are unable to support the original treatment, a temporary plan should be prepared to provide the lowest grade pay as defined in these measures with General Reserves, Common Righteousness Education Funds, or other sources of funding from other funds to fulfill the conditions as set in these measures. XVII. These measures shall be resolved by the Provincial Government Committee, promulgated, and implemented.

Jiangsu Provincial Education Institution Personnel Going Abroad for Research Examinations in Mid-August

Zhenjiang News: In order to encourage the staff of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Institution to study diligently, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education will, starting from the 20th year, annually examine current personnel of the provincial education institutions in the province who have graduated from colleges and universities and have served continuously for more than five years with achievements and who are natives of Jiangsu to go abroad for research. This year, it has been decided to select one person each (one in natural science and one in social science). Anyone who wishes to take this examination can ask the person in charge of their original institution to register with the Department of Education before August 15, and the physical examination will be held on August 16, and the examination will be held from August 17 to 19 (at Nanjing Central University). The examination subjects for general subjects are Party Principles, Chinese Language, Local History and Geography, and the Language of the Country of Study. The specialized examination subjects are: (1) Calculus, (2) University Physics, (3) Inorganic Chemistry, (4) Organic Chemistry, (5) Analytical Chemistry (for those who take the natural science examination), (1) Modern World History, (2) World Political Geography, (3) Educational Psychology, (4) Educational Administration (for those who take the social science examination). Candidates can choose three of the above two categories of specialized subjects for the examination. The calculation of examination results is that Party Principles, Chinese Language, and Local History and Geography in the general subjects account for 25% of the total score, the language of the country of study accounts for 25%, and specialized subjects account for 50%. After being admitted, they will be sent abroad for research, with a period of two years. The number of monthly allowances is regulated at (English) 30 pounds, (German) 350 marks, (French) 1,600 francs, and (American) 100 gold dollars. The cost of going abroad is 80 pounds for English, German, and French, and 400 gold dollars for American. However, because the price of gold has risen, there is no surplus for tuition, so starting from this year, it has been decided to stop issuing family allowances.

Commercial News

Finance: Fundamental Shakeup on Multiple Fronts - Gold Market Plunges - Result: Another $1.20 Loss

Yesterday, the market was even more sluggish, with the fundamental shakeup on multiple fronts becoming increasingly evident. Sellers dominated the market throughout the day, causing prices to fall to the 30 yuan mark, only one yuan away from the closing price. Initially, overseas silver markets showed a slight contraction in the UK and were flat in the US, with reports suggesting that there were buyers at the quoted price after the market closed. Sellers quoted prices above 0.062. Forward silver prices in Monterey rose by 5 hao, varying up to 2.5 li. The price of raw gold in London fell by half a penny, and exchange rates slightly decreased. The Central Bank's quoted prices were flat, and the Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. The standard gold price was quoted at 129 yuan, opening slightly lower. However, there were still many who were selling. The HSBC quoted prices were flat for both British and American currencies. At this time, spot dealers made slight advances but remained hesitant. After entering the market, the Silver Equalization Tax was revealed to be slightly less by half a point, and sellers took the opportunity to act, causing a further decline. However, large speculators bought in on the cheap, slightly pulling up the price. Ultimately, due to the fundamental shakeup on multiple fronts and oversupply, the price fell further to the 30 yuan mark at noon. Swap prices were quoted by buyers at 3 yuan to 3.1 yuan, while spot to September futures was quoted by buyers at 2.5 yuan. The market conditions for the first half of the day are recorded below.

Securities: A Sudden Surge - Class A Bonds Reach 70 Yuan - A Reversal Begins...Result Still Up 0.9 Yuan

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange began trading September futures. The market continued to trend upward. However, after rising too high, it triggered a slight reversal, resulting in a fleeting and volatile situation. Class A bonds reached 70 yuan, a sudden surge that seemed too rapid. This led many long positions to take profits and close out positions, causing a slight pullback after the large rise. The trend inevitably weakened. However, the uneven distribution of gains and losses showed that many were specializing in pushing up the price of Class A bonds in an attempt to deceive others. Although there is still an upward trend in the future, it is likely to be limited. If it can stabilize for a while, it would be fortunate for the long positions. Yesterday, the opening saw continued and strong upward momentum, which intensified even further later on. August Class A bonds surged by 1.25 yuan. September bonds, which were newly listed, immediately opened across the board and were even higher than the recent bonds, indicating that the long positions were very bullish. The excessive increase in Class A bonds led to an inverted yield curve, revealing a slight weakness, and a reversal began immediately. In the secondary market, numbers 48 and 51, as well as numbers 4, 33, 54, and others, were sold off one after another, causing a reversal to begin. Class E bonds were stable and did not rise, and the trend has changed its path, leading to a loss of confidence. Class B bonds fell by a maximum of 0.6 yuan, while Class A bonds only fell by a small 0.3 yuan, so the downward trend is not significant. As a result of yesterday's market prices, excluding the new September contracts, August contracts still saw a consistent increase of 0.35 to 0.9 yuan. The total transaction volume was 8,695,000 yuan. Today is the settlement day for the July futures, and the market is closed for one day. Yarn and Cotton: Many Scatter, Leaving the Market - Little Progress in the Yarn Market

The yarn market continues to decline, and the downward trend is particularly strong. This is because long positions have no intention of adding to their positions after settlement, and at the same time, a portion of the long positions are leaving the market, which makes the short positions feel more active, and the market is showing an increasingly strong downward trend. However, spot yarn transactions are gradually developing in the south, but market sentiment is still difficult to boost.

In the previous market for standard yarn, the market chips were loose, buyers were scarce, and sentiment was low. In addition, many rumors were circulating that were unfavorable to long positions. The market decline became increasingly severe, with each month falling by 1 yuan to 1.2 or 1.3 yuan. The second and third markets were sluggish. By closing, the decline in the distant months was even more severe. As a result, each month fell by 1.8 yuan compared to the closing price of the previous day. Under the Control of Natural Forces - More New Cotton is Being Dumped

The cotton market is experiencing a decline in old cotton, and the situation is extremely weak. This is due to the unfavorable market conditions, which are being controlled by natural forces. Therefore, the market price is becoming increasingly difficult to support. New cotton is being dumped more actively due to the favorable weather conditions and healthy growth. However, Indian cotton futures are gradually rising.

Osaka’s three-grade cotton fell by 6.7 jiao for near-term and 2.3 jiao for far-term. Market sentiment was very weak. Due to abundant rumors and favorable weather conditions, new cotton production is promising. Therefore, short sellers became very aggressive. The momentum of August old cotton became increasingly weak. As a result, old cotton fell by 1.5 yuan compared to the previous day’s closing price, while new cotton fell sharply by 4, 5, and 6 jiao. Cotton Mills Suspend Operations for Spot Cotton

The consumption of spot cotton remains suspended, and most factories are taking a wait-and-see attitude. The source of supply is Yao cotton, with 280 bales.

Increased Cotton Fields Near Taicang

This year, the cotton fields in Taicang and its surrounding areas have seen a large increase. This is because cotton prices have risen, and rural farmers are happy to plant cotton. Jiangyin County has increased by 20%, and other counties have increased by 10%. The total area of cotton fields is 1.56 million mu. The production status in all areas is exceptionally lush. If there are no typhoons or rainstorms to destroy the crops in the future, there should be a rare harvest in recent years.

US Cotton Falls, Indian Cotton Rises - Slight Declines in Three-Grade Yarn and Cotton

Yesterday, the US cotton market opened with good news from Liverpool. Brokers and foreign merchants bought, and Oklahoma experienced a lack of rain last week. All months rose by 18 to 22 points. Later, long positions closed out, and local New Orleans merchants and cotton farmers unanimously sold short. Oklahoma is forecast to have rain. Although there are storms near the Louisiana coast and the Bahamas, and there is rain in the central region, this could not reverse the downward trend. There were limited outside buyers, and most industry players took a wait-and-see approach to see how the new cotton would fare. Spot cotton was firm, and textiles became increasingly sluggish. The closing was flat and weak. Spot cotton fell by 7 points, and futures fell by 1 to 7 points. British cotton spot rose by 9 points, and futures rose by 4 to 10 points. Indian cotton spot merchants, Japanese merchants, and operators bought in large quantities. With long positions closing out, Pingguo rose by 2.75 rupees, Aomula rose by 3 rupees, and Bairo Creek rose by 2.25 to 3 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (telegram dated 27th).

According to a telegram from Bombay on the 28th, the opening forecast was: July-August Bairo Creek at 233 rupees, down 1.75 rupees; April-May Bairo Creek at 222 rupees, down 1.25 rupees; December-January Yimla at 201 rupees, down 1.75 rupees.

According to a telegram from Bombay on the 27th, the quantity of cotton exported from Rangoon last week totaled 535 tons, of which 25 tons went to Hamburg, 10 tons went to Antwerp, 482 tons went to Kobe, and 18 tons went to Melbourne.

According to a telegram from Osaka on the 28th, three-grade yarn futures fell by 0.1 to 0.4 yuan, with the near-term at 211.8 yuan and the far-term at 206.9 yuan. Cotton futures fell by 0.25 to 0.6 yuan, with the near-term at 69.6 yuan and the far-term at 65.9 yuan.

It was reported that a large quantity of spot cotton was shipped to Japan. However, due to good weather conditions, the market remained sluggish. More rain has been received and is still needed. Food: Northern Port Water Fees to Increase - Flour Alone Rises for August

Yesterday, the flour market was calm in the morning after the opening because this month has already been settled, so there should be no problems. For August and subsequent months, due to the quoted prices of foreign wheat, Chicago rebounded by 3, 4, or 5 jiao, and Canada was good by 4 jiao. Industry sentiment could not help but stabilize, and due to market rumors that water fees will increase from August 1st, Tianjin merchants have been rushing to load goods in recent days. The market has stabilized, which is likely due to this reason. For September and subsequent months, sentiment is naturally concerned about the abundant harvest of new rice in various places, and many long positions have retreated. The market atmosphere is generally flat and weak. After observing the subsequent movements, it is feared that the subsequent market will gradually decline.

Spot Merchants Frequently Hedge - Wheat Futures Gradually Soften

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw a slight stabilization of sentiment in the morning due to foreign wheat prices rising by 3, 4, or 5 jiao. However, the factory demand for ground wheat remained lukewarm, and customers with spot wheat frequently hedged, causing the market atmosphere to gradually weaken. As for the far-term contracts, the increase in value for each month was ultimately around 0.1 yuan, which was too large. Therefore, by comparison, sentiment gradually changed. The recent sharp drop in the far-term was not without reason. Although the spot wheat market remained nominally strong, it was actually loosening. This is because factories only accept very high-quality wheat, and anything below medium-quality is not purchased. The very high-quality wheat purchased by the factories yesterday ranged from 4.55 yuan to 4.5 yuan, with total transactions of over 3000 bags. However, it is reported that Japanese merchants purchased 8000 to 9000 bags of medium-quality wheat, with prices slightly higher than those purchased by Shanghai factories.

Delivery for July wheat futures is underway, and it is reported that over 20 railcars have already been delivered, with the total estimated at over 60 railcars.

Hakka Xian and Sichuan Merchants Expand Relief Efforts

There has been a continuous stream of Hakka Xian rice arriving in recent days, with many inferior grades. Merchants and retailers are eager to sell off their stocks. The middle-level firms are even willing to lower prices, as most of the inferior grades are generating heat and cannot be stored any longer. Furthermore, new rice has already been released in various places, and it is expected to arrive in Shanghai soon. The samples from various places are better than in previous years. Therefore, sentiment and market conditions continue to decline. Yesterday, the market initially showed signs of decline. However, Sichuan merchants suddenly made purchases in the market, which boosted the market. Furthermore, the Sichuan merchants are aiming to provide relief to the disaster-stricken areas of the province, and their demand is very high. They reportedly need to purchase and ship 200,000 shi in Shanghai and 100,000 shi in various ports along the Yangtze River. They are specifically selecting medium-grade rice for price stabilization and disaster relief. Yesterday, approximately 4000 bags were purchased, all of which were medium-to-inferior grade rice. The total volume of Jiangxi rice traded for the day was 5742 bags, and the total volume of Hunan rice traded was 1125 bags. Trading firms also distributed approximately 2000 bags themselves. In addition to Sichuan, there was also trade with local merchants and merchants from Zhejiang.

(Henan) Yesterday, a total of 16 or 17 shipments arrived from various sources (totaling over 3000 shi). The local market was sluggish. Only Qingdao merchants purchased over 600 bags. Therefore, market conditions continued to be weak. Prices for thick-grain early japonica rice and thin-grain rice only barely held steady for truly fresh goods. Medium-quality rice dropped nearly a jiao, and Du Yang jianyan dropped slightly. The price of Metasyn flat. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, 12 or 13 shipments arrived from various roads along the river. The market's demand for various goods remained sluggish. The price of white japonica rice continued to decline by several fen. The price of white Metasyn was stable, and the price of thin-grain rice was weak. Yangbu Hakka Xian, etc., were mostly steady, but sales remained weak. The prices of other goods were also weak.
