Chronicles

Odds and Ends

— (Zhou Liangchao)

A single lamp, small as a bean, in a humble room; its light is certainly faint, but it already possesses the function of providing utility to people. We only need to develop our abilities in ways that benefit society. We cannot say how great the effect will be, but I believe a comforting feeling in the heart can be reaped in abundance. Friends: do not despise the smallness of your own abilities. The spreading of lamplight is a symbol of vitality in each of our lives.

A small stick of ink; we should not underestimate that it has no great use. If we examine it closely, in terms of the progress of culture and the transmission of art, it is enough to be called a powerful force that "does not disgrace its mission." In this regard, we can learn a good lesson: that is, do not think that being utilized by others means being weak. People who are valuable and capable enough to be utilized by others are worthy of our praise and emulation.

The cicadas these days are exercising their authority to the full, their noisy chirping deafening, disturbing people's tranquility, and quite annoying. In reality, no benefit can be found in them. Why bother making such noise, inviting curses? A friend said to me: The cicadas' chirping is just a phenomenon during the scorching heat of summer and is not worth taking to heart. Moreover, their lifespan is so short. When summer ends and autumn comes, they will disappear without a trace.

Numbers

— Zhu Ying

Numbers are merely used to indicate the quantity or amount of qualities, quantities, or other various things. For example, a lawsuit, two slaps, three cobblers, and the like; there is originally nothing much to say about them. However, since numbers indicate the quantity or amount of qualities or quantities, then for the sake of indicating the quantity or amount of qualities or quantities, it is natural that if one doesn't speak, then so be it, but if one does speak, one should speak accurate numbers. For example, to say, "That woman is only twenty-two or twenty-three years old," "That time was in June or July," "Yesterday's rain started at four or five o'clock," "That was an article of three or four thousand words." This type of consecutive use of two numbers together is truly somewhat perplexing.

In the past, when I was in my hometown, when people spoke of the distance of a journey, there was almost a fixed pattern. The most common were the distances of "three li," "six li," "nine li," "twelve li," "eighteen li," "twenty-four li," "thirty-six li," "forty-eight li," and "sixty li." Although in reality, the length of the journey was often inconsistent, when speaking of it, people would always say the closest round number of li. No one ever said, "From such-and-such place to such-and-such place is twenty-seven li" or "twenty-eight li." Therefore, we could often hear people say, "The thirty-six li from Place A to Place B is much farther than the thirty-six li from Place B to Place C." Even the same "thirty-six li" could be distinguished as near or far; it was truly an indescribably subtle way of speaking.

In recent years, the uses of numbers have become wider and wider every day. In addition to their original use as adjectives, they have gradually transformed into pronouns or nouns. For example, the house number of the Wang residence is number thirteen, so "number thirteen" has become a pronoun for the Wang residence. The given name of the female tea server Yang Aidi is not well-known, but "number seven" is known by everyone to be that waitress with the expressive eyes and eyebrows. Patrolmen, mail carriers, ticket sellers on streetcars, and so on all seem to be hiding their names. Such-and-such number is someone's real name, which is really interesting. Furthermore, the various sections and divisions in government offices are now also replaced with numbers. When speaking of them, it's always Section One, Section Two; it's extremely simple. And in factories, there are even the glorious titles of "Namo Wen" and "Namo Tuo" (pronounced "Na Me Wen" and "Na Me Tuo," meaning number one, that is, the foreman, and number two, the assistant foreman), representing their real names. However, in Shanghai, there are some numbers that are not used as numbers. Such as "not three not four," "seven don't match eight," "don't care three seven twenty-one," "stir seven think three," "mouth five tongue six," "board board sixty-four," "six chaos three thousand," "nonsense three thousand," "two eight five," and so on. Even the world's top mathematicians would have no way to explain the logic of these numbers. But these numbers are so familiar to everyone in Shanghai that they flow out of their mouths naturally. Strange numbers indeed.

A Scene at the North Railway Station

— Zhang Muliang

The North Railway Station seems to be perpetually showing a noisy and chaotic scene, as if adhering to a schedule. This scene will absolutely never be erased from our impressions.

"Dang! Dang!..." After a series of loud bell strikes, that monster of the twentieth century, having crouched on the tracks and roared until hoarse, has arrived. Tall, short, thin, fat…people of all different shapes and sizes emerge from the dark train compartments, stirring about. Goods large and small are likewise stirring about. The clamor of voices, the tense emotions, everything is filled with hurried activity. The very cells of the crowd seem to be trembling in this noisy and chaotic scene.

Originally, there was only a traffic police officer standing at the entrance, but now the situation is clearly different. The armed police have increased from one to ten or so.

People, one by one, in strings, wriggle their way out at the ticket collection point. The police take advantage of this time to check people's bulky luggage.

"Sir! Nanjing Hotel is good, oh?" "Sir! The East Asia Hotel is very clean." The hotel greeters are all rushing to drum up business.

The rickshaw pullers standing outside the iron fence, seeing this situation, feel as if the greatest hope has arrived. So they use their swift legs, rushing to the station entrance to snatch up everyone's business. However, the rickshaw pullers' fate of doing business is ultimately blocked by the police officers' batons.

"Dang! Dang!..." After another series of loud bell strikes, the radio in the station reports loudly and clearly, "The Beijing-Shanghai 1:20 express train is about to depart!" As a result, the station, which had been quiet for a moment, returns to its chaotic state.

The North Railway Station seems to be perpetually showing a noisy and chaotic scene, as if adhering to a schedule. This scene will absolutely never be erased from our impressions.

When Drinking Water, Remember the Source

—

Changing Phoenix

Authored by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: Sight and Hearing Are Not Fleeting, Doubt Turns to Letter; Life and Death Can Be Entrusted, Generously Sending a Lament

It was not far from the school; turning into a small alley, he bumped right into the girl he did not wish to see. Today she had changed into a white top, tied with a long green lake crepe skirt. A jasmine ball hung diagonally on her coat button. In her hand she carried a small umbrella, but did not open it. Judging by her appearance, she seemed quite natural. A person with worries of his own connects events, thinking that she hadn't been angry? Just as he was thinking this, she seemed to have a new thought. She suddenly stopped and stared at him. Guoqi himself did not know how to behave properly, and his eyelids kept drooping down, not daring to look at her directly. At this time, she stopped and looked over, so he absolutely could not ignore her. He couldn't help but smile at her. At this moment, he saw that she was showing an unprecedented attitude, and she gave Guoqi a deep nod. However, after nodding, she had no other expression, immediately raised her head, and walked straight away. Guoqi, when leaving the school gate, made up his mind to ignore her, and his mind was much clearer. Now, having encountered her again, and having received this unexpected treatment, he could not help but be happy. Once happy, he unknowingly re-entered the maze. So, he resumed his pre-departure attitude, tucked the sachet under his arm, lowered the brim of his felt hat a little, and took the first step towards home. He walked straight into the front door, then woke up a second time, realizing he could not continue to be lost in wild thoughts. Standing still for a moment, as if in front of a mirror, he deliberately put on a smile, then walked into the hall with his chest puffed out. In fact, after that one admonition, Madam Zhang guessed that Guoqi would no longer take the matter of writing battles to heart. At this time, he was resting in his bedroom. Guoqi saw that there was no one in the hall, and did not want to disturb his mother again, so he quietly walked back to his own room. He didn't understand why, but he felt particularly tired. He fell onto the rattan chair and didn't even want to turn over. He lay like this for about an hour or two and did not get up until it was time for dinner. Liu Ma came to invite him to dinner. He wanted to refuse, but he was afraid that his mother would suspect he was ill, so he had to stand up and tidy his clothes. And he was afraid that his face would show signs of illness, so he wiped his face twice with a wet towel before going to the hall. He saw that what was on the table was a bowl of tofu soup, a bowl of boiled bok choy, a bowl of stir-fried string beans with shredded pork, and two small crucian carp. (54)

Biographical Sketches

The Life of Gorky (Part 2)

— Lin Liqin

In 1898, at the age of thirty, Gorky's first single-volume collection of short stories, "Makar Chudra," was published. In May of the same year, he was arrested for the second time and imprisoned in a fortress in the central part of the Outer Caucasus, charged with organizing criminal associations, conducting social democratic propaganda in workers' groups, and expressing dissatisfaction with the current system and government policies with the aim of overthrowing the imperial autocratic regime. However, he was soon acquitted without charges.

In 1900, he was arrested for the third time and exiled to the Alyaksamovsky district, accused of subsidizing insurgents. Later, with the assistance of Tolstoy and after an examination by seven doctors, it was proven that his lungs were unhealthy, and he was released.

In 1902, Gorky was elected as an honorary member of the Royal Academy of Sciences, but this recommendation aroused jealousy and opposition from a small number of aristocratic circles, who used the fact that Gorky had been accused of conducting revolutionary propaganda among workers and violating Article 1035 of the criminal law to revoke his qualification.

In 1903, at the age of thirty-five, "Gorky's Collected Works" in six volumes was published. In this year, Gorky bought a publishing house, published daily newspapers, and published many editorials advocating revolution, as well as many inexpensive popular literature readers.

In 1905, after the Russian Tsar massacred demonstrating crowds, Gorky was arrested again for drafting a "Declaration Attempting to Subvert the Existing Russian System," and as a result, he was exiled abroad.

In the spring of 1906, Gorky left Russia for the United States, where he gave speeches and held meetings to raise funds for the Russian revolutionary movement. He was forced to move to the island of Capri in Italy for a short stay. The following year, he went to England to attend the London Congress of the Social Democratic Party.

In 1908, Gorky organized a branch of the Social Democratic Party on the island of Capri in Italy and provided the party with most of his royalties. During this period, Gorky began corresponding with Lenin.

In 1914, during the tercentenary commemoration of the Romanov dynasty, Gorky had the opportunity to be pardoned and returned to Russia.

After the completion of the Russian October Revolution in 1917, Gorky devoted his best efforts and actively participated in the Soviet cultural construction.

In 1921, Gorky's old pulmonary tuberculosis illness relapsed, and he went to Sorrento, Italy, again to recuperate. The following year, he moved to Germany.

On March 19, 1928, Gorky's sixtieth birthday was celebrated. In the same year, it was also the thirty-fifth anniversary of Gorky's engagement in literary life. On this day, the entire Soviet Union held grand celebrations for him. In this month, Gorky returned to his country and was elected as a member of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union.

In the summer of 1931, Gorky rejoined the Bolshevik Party with the status of a formal party member.

In April 1932, in the year that the first Five-Year Plan of the Soviet Union was completed, on the eve of the start of the second Five-Year Plan, the All-Union Committee of Writers' Associations was established, and Gorky, with his reputation as a caregiver of proletarian literature, was elected as its honorary chairman.

In 1936, Gorky, at the age of sixty-seven, contracted the flu and died of illness on June 18 in a village near Moscow.

Looking at Gorky's life as a whole, the poverty of his early life and the spirit of his struggle with the environment in his middle age are truly admirable. And especially, he never received a day of systematic education and became a giant in the world of literature through self-study, how many people in history can compare!

Here, we want to talk about Gorky's literary tendencies. Regarding the exploration of this aspect, there is no need to say more. In a word, Gorky is a very progressive B-grade writer.

However, Gorky's early works tended towards romantic realism. Because he himself came from the lower classes, the characters in his novels were almost all rags and tatters. The original quality expressed by his core intention was to create a philosophy of transcending good and evil by deliberately portraying the rogue type with a strong will and passionate feelings due to the psychology of worshiping supermen and by satisfying the actions of destroying laws and social order. Such works include "Chelkash" and "Malva," etc. It was not until after 1898 that he changed this style.

Gorky's works can be roughly divided into five periods here:

The first period was from 1892 to 1898. This was the period when he created short stories, that is, the initial era of his tendency towards romance and realism.

The second period was from 1899 to 1906. This was the period when he wrote novels and plays about social issues. Important works during this period include the novel "Foma Gordeyev," "Three Men," and the plays "The Petty Bourgeoisie," "The Lower Depths," etc. During this period, Gorky founded a daily newspaper and wrote many editorials advocating revolution.

The third period was from 1907 to 1909. This was the period when he began to write novels depicting class struggles. The main works during this period include the play "Enemies" and the novel "Mother," etc.

The fourth period was from 1910 to 1912. This was the literary period when he bravely devoted himself to the revolutionary tide. During this period, he ruthlessly criticized the decline of the petty bourgeoisie and clearly supported the growth of the proletariat. The main works include the novella "Okurov City" and the novel "Matvei Kozhemyakin," etc.

The fifth period was from 1912 to the end of his last breath. During this long period, in addition to completing his great epic, "The Forties," it can be said that this was the period when he wrote autobiographies and memoirs. Works on autobiographies include "My Childhood" and "My Universities." Texts on memoirs include "Reminiscences of Andreyev" and "Reminiscences of Korolenko"—Korolenko was an early progressive writer in Russia. Gorky's rise to the literary world was greatly assisted by him—and other works. In addition, there is the play "Yegor Bulychov," etc.

Speaking of the origin of Gorky's literary success, this is due to his fundamental denial of metaphysics and theoretical propositions: he believes that the statement "When the cannon fires, the muse is silent" is extremely erroneous. Therefore, he resolutely threw two bombs into the garden of literature with his poems praising brave madness: "The Song of the Falcon" and "The Song of the Stormy Petrel," demanding that the storm come more forcefully. This was proven after the Russian October Revolution, and Gorky's literary success of course has his valuable arguments and viewpoints.

The great Gorky, whom we admire and serve, has left this world. This is the greatest misfortune of the world literary scene and an irreparable loss! I said this at the beginning. However, death is the inevitable end of life, and the phrase "eternal life" is as vague in the philosophy of life as "God." We can only push to the point of "the dead are already dead," put away our sadness for Gorky, and look forward to the new Gorky coming to this world!

Essays

The Spanish Unrest

— Xiang

Spanish women are world-renowned for their beauty, but few know that their people are in dire straits. The revolutionary tide has been very strong in recent years. Spain was originally a kingdom. In the 1931 revolution, the emperor was overthrown and a republic was established. However, their landlord forces were very powerful. Therefore, although the throne representing the interests of the landlords was overthrown, the landlord forces still existed. In recent years, they have stood in two sharp opposing camps with the revolutionary forces. This unrest is still the work of the old forces. According to a dispatch from the National News Agency in Paris on the 24th, the deposed King Alfonso of Spain told reporters from the Paris Evening News today that he did not want to return to the country immediately, and said that if the leftist government continued to cling to power, this revolution (!) would never end. He deeply wished that Spain would get rid of terror and slaughter (?) Only the failure of the leftist government could end the civil war and bring peace to Spain (!) This revolution is purely a national movement (!) that is, the joint active action of royalists and right-wing republicans to overthrow the leftist government. The deposed emperor's remarks could not have made the content of the Spanish unrest clearer.

In addition, according to a dispatch from Havas News Agency in Madrid on the same day, the government recently issued a radio broadcast stating that the money used by the rebels was provided by the financier March, who is a well-known Spanish banker. When the restorationist leader General Sanjurjo launched an uprising in 1932, he secretly provided funds, which led to him being sentenced to imprisonment. He then found a way to escape and lived abroad. From all aspects, we can see how landlords, bankers, the deposed emperor representing the landlords, and imperialists have, in fact, formed a united front, each doing their best to severely suppress the revolutionary wave that Spain has seen in recent centuries. This example has been demonstrated too much and too thoroughly in the past and present history. Looking at it today, we feel particularly close and insightful! The various wounds we have suffered, in the context of the fierce struggle between revolution and counter-revolution in Spain, are truly worth stroking and receiving some new lessons.

In a corner of Southern Europe, the beacon of moving from the old society to the new society has been burning brightly since the beginning of this century. In the Far East continent, China is also staging a state of unease caused by being trampled on by imperialists. Do not neglect our current position and strength. In the rapidly changing history of the world, we are shouldering the most important responsibilities and missions.

A Kind Woman

— Menghua

It was dusk, and it was raining lightly. I was walking alone with an umbrella, feeling lost. After turning a small alley, a familiar house appeared before my eyes.

Seeing this house, for some reason, my heart suddenly tightened. I took gentle steps, as if afraid of disturbing someone, and my heart beat rapidly. I carefully observed every passerby in front and behind, and they were all shrinking as they walked, which made me feel a little relieved. So I knocked on the door with my trembling palm.

I was afraid that a stranger would come out. What would I say then? And what if she already had guests? These questions swirled in my mind. But I didn't want to leave. I knocked on the door again.

Someone answered from inside! My God, it better be her. But the door felt as distant as a mountain, and I couldn't hear clearly if the voice inside was her. I almost wanted to slip away, but just then the door creaked open. It was her, no doubt, it was her. So I didn't dare to even look her in the face and, like someone who had just recovered from a serious illness, weakly lifted my right foot and crossed the threshold.

"I was just about to go out!" My mind gradually calmed down. I raised my head and looked at her. She was waiting for my reply, and her eyes were like fire, burning me all over.

"You didn't expect me to come, did you?" I said, my voice trembling.

She nodded and poured me a cup of tea. So we sat face to face.

Seeing her, I was once again immersed in the ocean of memories. I remembered it was also a rainy night, and it was already late. I was walking alone, running home along that mysterious street. Suddenly, a ghost-like figure came over and asked me in a low voice:

"Come to my house and have some fun!"

I looked at her in surprise. In the dim light, I saw two strings of tears glistening on her pale cheeks. I was stunned. Just then, she came closer and took my hand.

"Have pity on me, I: I..." She seemed unable to say anything more. So I didn't even reply and walked with her into this house where I was now sitting.

I saw a woman whose body had been defiled but who had a kind soul. This woman was her. She had brought me something mysterious. She was like a riddle, a knot that would never be untied. So tonight, I had come back here again with a sense of danger.

She was so reluctant to speak! Even a sentence seemed to require a long period of thought. Sitting in front of me was the Sphinx, I felt.

"Is your illness a little better?" I remembered what she had told me last time and asked her like that.

She shook her head. I saw her panting slightly, her hands pressing against her heaving chest, but she couldn't cough. "I don't fall asleep until one or two o'clock every night, and I can't sleep well... Alas, is there any hope for it to get better?" Like a lullaby sung by a mother holding her dead child, the trembling voice sounded mournfully.

I ran over and put my hand on her shoulder. I felt an awkward temptation, but it was pure. But she suddenly shook my hand off, turned her head, and said:

"Why did you come again? If I had known you were this kind of person, I would have regretted treating you wrongly that night... This is not a place for you to come, brother..."

It seemed that only crying could express the pain in her heart, and a series of tears streamed down. Under the lamplight, the tear-filled eyes flickered like the lake water under the slanting rays of the setting sun, so desolate.

I hugged her tightly and completely fainted.

"If I had a relative... just one, then I would..." she sobbed. "But all the people I meet every day are beasts, pigs, and dogs. They treat me so cruelly..." She raised her head and asked me with a prayerful expression: "People say there is no mountain that cannot be crossed in this world. Is that true? When will I be able to cross this mountain? Haven't I suffered enough yet? I'm really tired, but I still have to drag myself down, and will it only be over when I die? Tell me! Tell me!" She shook my shoulders hard. "Why don't you say anything? You!"

I saw the flames of hope burning fiercely in her heart. But all of life was constantly pouring water on it. Wasn't life already weariness and loathing to her?

The night was getting deeper, and the four walls were triumphantly raising the sound of mahjong, the noise, and the lewd laughter. My whole body was as uncomfortable as if it was being pricked by needles. We were all in the desert, feeling an indescribable loneliness.

We could only sit, sit, timidly and piously waiting for dawn.

Physiognomy of a Camel

— You Qi

In order to save expenses, I moved into a large compound. At first, I wasn't used to it, but gradually, I got used to it.

In the afternoon, the sun was blocked by the western gable, and the alley was a bit shady. "What a great opportunity!" The belief jumped into everyone's heart. The elder sister-in-law from the back building, the aunt from the front building, and all sorts of people rushed out of their cages. The clothes were also quite grand. Sitting, standing, talking, laughing, all were indulged in naturally, without any restraint.

Two women walked in at the entrance. Judging by appearance, they were both over forty years old. Their feet were bound, and they walked a bit crookedly. The black leather bags looked quite heavy.

"We do physiognomy, all kinds of physiognomy." She swept her eyes over everyone, "even camel physiognomy."

Many eyes were fixed on her face, body, and feet. The older sister from next door added jokingly:

"How much for one physiognomy reading?"

"One dollar for a detailed reading, 150 copper coins for a regular reading."

"150 copper coins isn't much. Just read it once, and we'll talk later." (To be continued)

Lotus

— Liao Chuxiu

I have already forgotten the Indian transliteration of the word "lotus." I used to know it. This flower is probably very common in India and is also highly valued. Shakyamuni sat on a lotus throne, and people in Zen Buddhism even used the number of layers on the lotus throne to distinguish the levels of hierarchy. In addition, the famous classic "The Lotus Sutra" explains that human beings are originally born in the mud, but they can bloom clean flowers.

As for my love for the lotus, I have already mentioned it in the previous article: the first reason is because its petals can be

Page 19

fried in flour and eaten. Later, after reading a little more miscellaneous books, I learned that tea leaves can be wrapped in thin silk, placed in newly opened lotus flowers overnight, and then taken out to brew and drink the next day, which has a special fragrance. I tried it occasionally, and it was indeed very good, but drinking it often is just so-so.

There are too many writings about lotus in old Chinese poems and lyrics, but Western literature mostly writes about water lilies. Water lilies are slightly less common than lotuses, and white ones are more common. Now, thanks to trade, they can also be seen in China.

It is best to plant lotuses naturally in a pond. Those planted in tanks are not very easy to grow big, and some Chinese people even plant them in small pots, with leaves the size of a palm and flowers the size of a wine glass, called pot lotuses. It is said that this kind of pot lotus is still grown from ordinary lotus seeds, but using a special method.

There is a kind of giant lotus in India that is almost four or five times larger than the Chinese lotus. Small children a few months old can sit in the open flower. This is probably not just a legend!

The Southern Dynasties' "Midnight Songs" and "Wu Songs" are a unique highlight in Chinese literature. These short poems about lotus are very good, but those passionate men and women do not have a special love for lotus flowers, but because the word "lian" (蓮) in "lotus" has the same sound as the "lian" (憐) in "ailian" (愛憐), meaning "cherish," taking its double meaning. "Midnight Songs" and "Wu Songs" are all folk songs. This situation can also be seen in later folk songs. The famous line "When lotus flowers wither, lotus seeds are seen" still cannot but move people deeply when read today. As for "Splitting open the lotus seed reveals much bitterness," it is even more poignant!

It's summer now, and it's the season when lotus flowers are in full bloom. I don't know where there are many lotus flowers blooming in Shanghai. "Leaving behind the withered lotus to listen to the sound of rain," I probably can only go somewhere to listen to the sound of rain on the withered lotus when the autumn rain is continuous.

Correction: There were quite a few errors in the article "A Visit to the Shanghai Frog Farm" published yesterday. For example, each frog can produce 10,000 eggs, and at least 8,000 to 9,000 of these 10,000 eggs can hatch into new frogs. The word "thousand" was omitted. A small difference makes a great error. After the author sent a letter pointing out the errors, we are correcting them immediately and apologize for the errors.

Miscellaneous Notes on "Hearts United in Life and Death"

"Hearts United in Life and Death" is the first work of the Second Studio of the Star Film Company.

The screenwriter of "Hearts United in Life and Death" is Mr. Yang Hansheng, the director is Mr. Ying Yunwei, and the leading actors are Yuan Muzhi and Chen Boer.

"Hearts United in Life and Death" is a work with the Northern Expedition as its historical background and the anti-warlord revolutionary movement as its theme.

"Hearts United in Life and Death" has two miniatures of the most progressive Chinese youths in contemporary society, as well as a girl who dedicates herself to practical revolutionary work.

In "Hearts United in Life and Death", Yuan Muzhi is sentenced to life imprisonment for participating in the revolution, escapes due to a fire in the prison, and is arrested again for participating in practical work, suffers torture, and is executed by firing squad.

"Hearts United in Life and Death" is a work in which Ying Yunwei collaborates with Yuan Muzhi again after "Song of the Peach and Plum."

"Hearts United in Life and Death" will begin filming at the Second Studio's photography studio immediately, and is scheduled to meet us after the autumn.

News Snippets from "Mr. Wang's Knight Errant Biography"

Tang Jie, the actor who plays "Mr. Wang," said, "Mr. Wang's Knight Errant Biography" is indeed more interesting than the previous "Mr. Wang" films, and there are many more jokes, and every joke is not nonsensical!

Cao Xuesong, "Little Chen," listened to Xian Xinghai directing the collection of the "Mr. Wang's Knight Errant Biography" theme song "Song of a Casual Laborer" record at the Pathé Company the other day and was greatly moved. He said: Listening to Mr. Xian's music, it's as if I'm right there on the pier, personally hearing those dockworkers who work like oxen and horses humming and heaving as they transport goods. I was moved, I was greatly moved, I have never heard such great music!

Director Zuo Ming not only responsibly guides the leading actors in their acting, but even if the extras are not good and don't know how to act, it will definitely affect the entire film.

Li Lin, "Little A Yuan," has fewer scenes in "Mr. Wang's Knight Errant Biography," but she works very hard, so the results are not bad!

Performing at the Great New World Amusement Park soon

Shanghai Local Supplement Automobile Weekly

New Information on Overseas Car Races

— Yun

Recent automobile races held in various places. The more important ones, such as the Italian Grand Prix and the American Memorial Day Race, are matters of concern to the automotive industry. Therefore, I have compiled a summary as follows.

Car Race Held in Italy

The winner of the Nice Automobile Grand Prix held in Italy this time was Tazio Nuvolari. (The race distance was 200 miles. Nuvolari's average speed was 104.241 kilometers (equivalent to 65.15 miles per hour). The three British drivers who participated in the race, Louis Martin and Hugh Hamilton, withdrew due to obstacles encountered during the race. Hugh Hamilton's luck was the worst. He was driving an Alfa Romeo car. He was only ten laps away from the finish line, and the time difference between him and the first place, Nuvolari, was only three minutes. It is a pity that the engine failed and he was forced to withdraw. The audience, seeing that Hugh Hamilton's situation was unavoidable, cheered to show their support. This was enough to make the brave man feel a little relieved. Martin drove a Bugatti car and reached the 32nd lap. The clutch suddenly broke, so he had to leave the field. Louis stopped driving in the 40th lap due to a failure of the igniter. He was driving a Maserati car. As a result, out of the eighteen starters in the race, only six finished the race. The famous Italian driver Varzi won the prize with an Auto Union car of 1,500 cubic centimeters. His average speed in 20 laps was 139.402 kilometers per hour. His time was three hours, forty-three minutes, forty-five and two-fifths seconds. Rosemeyer was the runner-up. He also drove an Auto Union car, with a speed of 137.317 kilometers per hour in three hours and forty-seven and seven-tenths seconds. Brivio was third. He drove an Alfa Romeo car, with a time of three hours, fifty-one minutes, fifty-one and four-fifths seconds. The average speed was 133.523 kilometers per hour. The most exciting part of the car race was when Varzi's strong opponent, Nuvolari, withdrew after running 13 laps due to engine failure.

Briton Wins Car Race Championship

British car racing expert Richard Seaman recently won the championship in the 1,500 cubic centimeter car class in the Coppa Acerbo car race held in Pescara. Seaman was driving an ERA car. In the first four laps, he led his 26 rivals. The audience cheered him for his superb driving skills and his majestic posture. The distance of four laps was 64 miles. The speed per hour was 127.128 kilometers (equivalent to 80 miles per hour). His time was forty minutes and forty-two and two-fifths seconds. Seaman's fastest run was in the second lap, which he completed in twelve minutes and two seconds. The average speed was 128.569 kilometers per hour. The other two British car drivers were both defeated by Seaman. Bouts drove an MG and finished seventh. His average speed was 120.654 kilometers per hour. The time was fifty-six minutes, seven and one-fifth seconds. Evans also drove an MG car and withdrew after the first lap due to engine failure. Seaman's first rival, de Farnary, drove a Maserati car and also stopped driving after the first lap. Below Seaman was Italian car racer Bonzo, driving a Maserati car. His time was forty-nine minutes, fifty-two and one-fifth seconds. The average speed was 124.162 kilometers. Third was Stiffey, who drove a Bugatti car. His time was fifty-one minutes, nineteen and one-fifth seconds. The average speed was 120.654 kilometers.

Manufacturing Cars for the Masses

— Song

There will be no radical reforms in cars in the future. Car sales in the United States increased in May.

Regarding the issue of future car styles, American car manufacturers unanimously tend towards streamlining. However, no one can say for sure to what extent streamlining should go. When it comes to the position of the engine, everyone believes that the trend of moving it to the rear has become an undeniable fact. Therefore, future cars will be particularly streamlined in appearance, and the engine will be moved to the rear. This trend is almost unanimously recognized by the automotive industry. However, I must say this again. If we carefully investigate the production center of American cars, Detroit, we can know that the innovations in cars in the next two or three years will not be overly sharp or overly radical. The reason is that radical changes place too much responsibility on the car companies. No one wants to take this risk.

Mr. Chrysler, General Manager of the American Pontiac Motor Company, recently expressed the above meaning. He went on to say that all car companies' plans for future new cars, all styles, engines, etc., must be shifted according to the habits of the masses. Therefore, future cars will be what drivers and passengers "want," not just what car companies want. Therefore, there will be no unusually radical reforms in the 1937 model cars in the major car factories. Mr. Chrysler also made an analogy, saying that if Pontiac built a 1937 model new car with a rear engine, everyone would naturally flock to the dealer's showroom to visit. However, as a result, not many people would want to buy it because many people would wait to see the results after others use it before daring to buy it.

Also, according to Mr. Chrysler, car companies want to know whether their annual car reforms are too radical. On this point, they focus most on the public's intentions. What they worry about is that the reforms are too novel and too far away from the public. The "penetration" problem of the car market aroused Mr. Chrysler's enthusiasm. He said that those who ask whether the car market is saturated are as foolish as those who ask whether the wheelbarrow is full because no one knows which answer is correct. The number of cars in Los Angeles has already exceeded 800,000, with an average of two cars for every three people. According to this ratio, the United States should currently have 83,000,000 cars, instead of the most generous estimate of 26,000,000. But who dares to say that it can never reach 83,000,000? Mr. Chrysler went on to say that, of course, before that number is reached, road engineering and road construction must undergo complete changes. What is needed now is not to obtain a large amount of roads with a small amount of money, but to obtain better roads with larger expenditures.

Recently, the number of car sales in various parts of the United States has been increasing, which shows that the renewal of the public's purchasing power is not false. Passenger car sales in May were only slightly higher than in April. In May, Chevrolet dealers sold a total of 129,816 passenger cars and trucks, completing the best record in three months. From January to May of this year, Chevrolet's sales were 535,634. Pontiac sold 21,278 cars in May, becoming a record that exceeded the crowd's expectations. Walter Chrysler's sales were 24,057 in May.

Buick's sales in May of this year were the best since 1928, totaling 17,689. Hudson's sales in May were similar to April's. According to its dealers' reports, a total of 60,764 were sold. The period was from January to May. Terraplane car sales are also included. Studebaker's sales in May were 8,705, which is almost the same as the 10,773 passenger cars and trucks sold in May 1929. In the past five months, its total sales were 40,008. Sales in the same period in 1929 were 50,533. Packard's sales in May exceeded the previous record, totaling over 7,200. Total sales this year have exceeded 27,000. The level of car sales will gradually decrease in the summer. This is the case every year. Business in rural areas usually improves in the summer. Currently, the weekly production of each car factory is 100,000 cars. This will gradually decrease in the future. Cars with current popular styles will be assembled by August 1st, but some companies will work until mid-August before stopping.

The trend of installing radios in cars is becoming more and more popular. According to recent estimates, the number of cars in the United States equipped with radios has exceeded 3,000,000. The proportion of new cars equipped with radios is increasing even more. Taking Chevrolet as an example, the percentage of new cars equipped with radios has increased from 15% to 22.5%. Chevrolet's management believes that having a radio in the car is a kind of enjoyment for drivers while riding, so they decided to set up a service department, with the general manager personally in charge of the matter. Under him, there are nine regional service managers to help dealers in various places promote the convenience of radio services.

Pontiac Sales Soar

According to reliable information, the number of retail sales of Pontiac cars in the United States was the highest in May. It ranks third among any May in the company's history. As for since 1929, there has never been a month with so many sales. The total number of retail sales of Pontiac cars in May of this year was 21,278. In April of last year, it was 19,481, and in May it was 16,209, both of which were far less. In the last ten days of May this year, Pontiac sold a total of 8,294. Compared with the sales for the entire month a year ago, this is an increase of 50%. According to Pontiac cars, since its debut, the sales in May of only 1928 and 1929 were more than in May of this year. As of June 1, a total of 104,997 Pontiac cars of the 1936 model have been delivered. As for the 1935 model a year ago, it was 66,985.

A Week's Record of Car Accidents

— San Yuan

There were a total of eight car accidents this week. One man died from serious injuries, three men were seriously injured, one man and one woman were slightly injured, and there was one case of mutual collision and property damage.
